Divine Attributes
beginner
4 min
Avoiding Theological Depth on Divine Attributes
Author states his commitment to avoid theological analysis of divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author chooses to avoid theological debates about divine attributes and instead follows the approach of the majority of Muslims.

Core Idea
Faith does not require philosophical analysis of God's attributes.

The author begins by outlining his methodology. His first commitment is to steer clear of deep theological debates about the nature of divine attributes—whether they are identical to God's essence or distinct. Instead, he advocates a simple, faithful approach: affirm what Allah has attributed to Himself and leave the rest. This lesson explains why he takes this stance and what it means for the believer.

Guided Path
1
Read the author's methodological principle
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the author lists this as his first commitment among several.
The phrase 'الابتعاد عن الخوض' (avoiding delving) is key.
2
Identify the debate being avoided
The author mentions the debate over whether attributes are identical to the essence ('عين الذات') or not. Understand that this was a major theological dispute between Ash'aris, Maturidis, and Mu'tazila.
The author follows 'جمهور المسلمين' (majority of Muslims), which is the Ash'ari/Maturidi stance, but he does not analyze it.
3
Understand the author's justification
He argues that a sensible Muslim need not engage in this debate. It is sufficient to affirm the attributes of perfection that Allah ascribes to Himself. He says this research is 'لا طائل فيه' (without benefit) for the common believer.
This is a practical, not a theological, argument.
4
Reflect on the limits of this avoidance
Note that the author says this is acceptable 'على أنه لا توجد ثمة أي شبهة في الإيمان بالله يتوقف ردها على الخوض في هذا البحث' — meaning, as long as no doubt in faith depends on resolving this issue. So if a doubt arises that requires this analysis, one may need to engage.
This is a nuanced position, not total rejection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد التزمت الأمور التالية في كتابة هذه البحوث :
أولاً ـ الابتعاد عن الخوض في حقيقة الصفات الإلهية وتحليلها وهل هي عين الذات أم غيرها ، وما يترتب على كل منهما ، مكتفياً باتباع مذهب جمهور المسلمين في ذلك . إذ يسع المسلم العاقل أن لا يفكر في ذلك أصلاً وأن لا يلتزم إلا ما نسبه الله تعالى إلى نفسه من صفات الكمال، على أنه لا توجد ثمة أي شبهة في الإيمان بالله يتوقف ردها على الخوض في هذا البحث الذي لا طائل فيه .
And I have committed to the following matters in writing these researches: First — avoiding delving into the reality of the divine attributes and their analysis, and whether they are identical to the essence or other than it, and what follows from each, contenting myself with following the doctrine of the majority of Muslims in that. For it is sufficient for the sensible Muslim to not think about that at all and to commit to nothing except what Allah Almighty has attributed to Himself of attributes of perfection, provided that there is no doubt in belief in Allah whose refutation depends on delving into this research that has no benefit.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a statement of methodological principle. The author lists three commitments; this is the first. He commits to avoiding the theological debate about the nature of divine attributes — specifically whether they are identical to the essence or distinct — and the implications of each view. He follows the majority (jumhur) of Muslims, which is the Ash'ari or Maturidi position that attributes are neither identical nor separate in a literal sense, but he avoids analysis. He argues that a sensible Muslim need not engage in this debate; it is sufficient to affirm the attributes Allah ascribes to Himself, as long as no doubt in faith depends on resolving this issue. He deems this research 'فيه لا طائل' (without benefit) for the common believer.

Key Terms
الصفات الإلهية
عين الذات
جمهور المسلمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author completely rejects any discussion of divine attributes.
Correction: The author only avoids such discussion when no doubt in faith depends on resolving the issue; if a doubt arises, engagement may be necessary.

Checkpoint
What is the author's first methodological commitment regarding divine attributes?
A) To prove that they are identical to the essence
B) To avoid delving into whether they are identical to the essence or not
C) To analyze them in detail
D) To follow the Mu'tazila view

Key Takeaway
The author avoids theological analysis of divine attributes, deeming it unnecessary for the lay believer, unless a doubt in faith requires it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt disturbed by doubts about Allah's attributes? When that happens, do you tend to analyze them intellectually, or do you trust what Allah has revealed about Himself? Which response aligns with the author's advice, and what would you need to change in your own approach?
?
The author says it is sufficient for a sensible Muslim not to think about these matters at all. Is there a part of you that resists this simplicity—that feels you must know more to be secure in your faith? What would it cost you to lay down that need and simply affirm Allah's names and attributes as He described them?
?
If you were to take the author's condition seriously—'provided that there is no doubt'—how would you honestly assess your own heart? Are there hidden doubts you are avoiding by not delving into these issues, or are you engaging in theological discussions out of intellectual curiosity rather than necessity? What would it mean for you to stop if no doubt exists?

Classification of Divine Attributes: The Psychological Attribute
Introduces classification and defines the psychological attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the division of God's attributes into four categories and the specific meaning of the psychological attribute as existence.

Core Idea
God's attributes are categorized to clarify His perfect essence.

This passage begins the systematic study of God's attributes. It first establishes that God possesses all perfections and is free from all deficiencies. Then it introduces a classification of twenty principal attributes into four categories, beginning with the psychological attribute, which is existence itself.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the General Principle
Read the opening statement that God is characterized by every attribute of perfection and free from deficiency, and understand why this is necessary based on His divinity.
This principle underlies all discussions of divine attributes.
2
Learn the Four Categories
Identify the four categories mentioned: psychological, negative, attributes of meanings, and conceptual attributes. Note that these cover all twenty principal attributes.
Each category will be explained in subsequent lessons.
3
Understand the Psychological Attribute
Focus on the definition of the psychological attribute as a positive attribute that indicates the essence without an additional meaning, and recognize that it is only existence. Note that it is not separate from God's essence.
This clarifies a common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثانيا: صفات الله تعالى. يجب أن تعلم في كلمة جامعة مجملة ، أن الله عز وجل متصف بكل صفات الكمال ، ومنزه عن جميع صفات النقصان . إذ إن ألوهيته تستلزم اتصافه بالكمال المطلق لزوماً بيناً بالمعنى الأخص. ثم إن علينا بعد ذلك أن نقف على تفصيل أهم هذه الصفات ، ونبين معناها ، وماتستلزمه من أمور ومعتقدات . وقد وصف الله تعالى نفسه في كتـابـه الكريم بصفات كثيرة مختلفة ، إلا أن جزئيات هذه الصفات كلها تلتقي عشرين صفة رئيسية ثبتت بدلالة الكتاب وبالبراهين القاطعة. وقد قسموا هذه الصفات إلى أربعة أقسام هي : الصفة النفسية ، الصفات السلبية ، صفات المعاني ، الصفات المعنوية . آ - الصفة النفسية. ضمن. والمراد بها صفة ثبوتية يدل الوصف بها على الذات دون معنى زائد عليهـا ككون الجوهر جوهراً وكونه شيئاً موجوداً . والصفة النفسية صفة واحدة هي ( الوجود ) ، وقد تحدثنا عنها بما يُغني عن إعادة البحث فيها ، فقد ثبت لك بالأدلة المختلفة السابقة وجود الله عز وجل ، وذلك هو الدليل على اتصافه بهذه الصفة ، إذ هى كما قلنا ليس شيئاً غير ذاته سبحانه وتعالى
Secondly: The Attributes of Allah Almighty. You must know in a comprehensive concise statement that Allah Almighty is characterized by every attribute of perfection and is free from all attributes of deficiency. For His divinity necessitates His being characterized by absolute perfection with an evident necessity in the most specific sense. Then, after that, we must stop at the detail of the most important of these attributes, and explain their meaning, and what they entail of matters and beliefs. And Allah Almighty has described Himself in His Noble Book with many different attributes, but all the particulars of these attributes converge on twenty principal attributes established by the evidence of the Book and by decisive proofs. And they have divided these attributes into four sections: (1) the psychological attribute, (2) the negative attributes, (3) the attributes of meanings, (4) the conceptual attributes. A - The psychological attribute: [ضمن] And it is meant by it a positive attribute whose description indicates the essence without an additional meaning, like the existence of a substance being a substance and being an existent thing. And the psychological attribute is one attribute: existence. And we have already spoken about it sufficiently to avoid repeating the research on it, for the existence of Allah Almighty has been established to you by the various previous proofs, and that is the evidence for His being characterized by this attribute, for it is, as we said, nothing other than His Essence, glorified and exalted.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage introduces the topic of the attributes of God. It begins by stating a fundamental principle: God is characterized by every attribute of perfection and is free from all attributes of deficiency, because His divinity necessarily entails absolute perfection. Then it says that we need to detail the most important attributes. The attributes found in the Quran are many, but they reduce to twenty principal attributes established by the Quran and decisive proofs. These twenty attributes are divided into four categories: (1) the psychological attribute (الصفة النفسية), (2) the negative attributes (الصفات السلبية), (3) the attributes of meanings (صفات المعاني), and (4) the conceptual attributes (الصفات المعنوية). The passage then explains the first category: the psychological attribute. It is a positive attribute that indicates the essence itself without any additional meaning, like the existence of a substance. There is only one such attribute: existence (الوجود). The author notes that the proof of God's existence has already been given in previous discussions, and that existence is not something separate from God's essence.

Key Terms
صفات
كمال
نقصان
ألوهية
صفة نفسية
وجود
صفات سلبية
صفات المعاني
صفات معنوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that the psychological attribute is a separate quality added to God's essence.
Correction: The psychological attribute (existence) is not an additional attribute; it is the essence itself. God's existence is nothing other than His own being.

Checkpoint
How many principal attributes does the author mention, and how are they categorized?
A) 20 attributes in 4 categories
B) 10 attributes in 2 categories
C) 7 attributes in 3 categories
D) 99 attributes in 4 categories

Key Takeaway
The psychological attribute is existence itself, which is not separate from God's essence but is His very reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's divinity requires absolute perfection, then every decision He makes for you is perfect. In what area of your life right now are you resisting His decree because it doesn't feel perfect? Will you today surrender that area to Him?
?
The passage says existence is not something added to God; He is existence itself. Your own existence is a gift from Him every moment. When was the last time you thanked Him not just for what He gave you, but for the sheer fact that He allows you to exist? How can you make that gratitude a daily practice?

Classification of Divine Attributes and the Attribute of Self
Buti classifies divine attributes and defines the attribute of Self.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four categories of divine attributes and the specific nature of the attribute of Self (existence) as identical to God's essence.

Core Idea
Divine attributes are divided into four types, with existence as the attribute of Self identical to His essence.

This passage lays the foundation for studying God's attributes. Buti begins by affirming God's absolute perfection, then introduces the twenty principal attributes divided into four categories. We focus here on the first category: the attribute of Self, which is existence itself — not a separate quality but identical to the essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the author's flow from a general statement to a detailed classification.
The passage uses a logical structure: necessity of perfection → need for detailing attributes → classification.
2
Identify the four categories
The passage lists four kinds of attributes: attribute of Self, negative attributes, attributes of meanings, and attributes entailed by meanings. Write them down and note the difference between the first one and the others.
3
Understand the attribute of Self
Focus on the definition: it's a positive attribute that indicates the essence without an additional meaning. The only such attribute is existence, which is not separate from God's essence.
This refutes the misconception that existence is a quality added to God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجب أن تعلم في كلمة جامعة مجملة ، أن الله عز وجل متصف بكل صفات الكمال ، ومنزه عن جميع صفات النقصان . إذ إن ألوهيته تستلزم اتصافه بالكمال المطلق لزوماً بيناً بالمعنى الأخص · ثم إن علينا بعد ذلك أن نقف على تفصيل أهم هذه الصفات ، ونبين معناها ، وماتستلزمه من أمور ومعتقدات . وقد وصف الله تعالى نفسه في كتابه الكريم بصفات كثيرة مختلفة ، إلا أن جزئيات هذه الصفات كلها تلتقي عشرين صفة رئيسية ثبتت بدلالة الكتاب وبالبراهين القاطعة وقد قسموا هذه الصفات إلى أربعة أقسام هي : الصفة النفسية ، الصفات السلبية ، صفات المعاني ، الصفات المعنوية . آ - الصفة النفسية والمراد بها صفة ثبوتية يدل الوصف بها على الذات دون معنى زائد عليها ككون الجوهر جوهراً وكونه شيئاً موجوداً . والصفة النفسية صفة واحدة هي ( الوجود ) ، وقد تحدثنا عنها بما يُغني عن إعادة البحث فيها ، فقد ثبت لك بالأدلة المختلفة السابقة وجود الله عز وجل ، وذلك هو الدليل على اتصافه بهذه الصفة ، إذ هى كما قلنا ليس شيئاً غير ذاته سبحانه وتعالى
You must know, in a comprehensive and concise statement, that God Almighty is described with every attribute of perfection, and is free from all attributes of deficiency. Because His divinity necessitates His being described with absolute perfection, a clear entailment in the most specific sense. Then after that, we must pause to detail the most important of these attributes, explain their meaning, and what they entail of matters and beliefs. And God Almighty has described Himself in His noble Book with many different attributes, except that the particulars of all these attributes converge into twenty principal attributes that are established by the evidence of the Book and by definitive proofs. And they divided these attributes into four sections: the attribute of Self, the negative attributes, attributes of meanings, and the attributes that are entailed by meanings. A - The attribute of Self: what is meant by it is a positive attribute whose description indicates the essence without an additional meaning, like the essence being a substance and being an existent thing. And the attribute of Self is one attribute: existence. And we have spoken about it sufficiently to dispense with repeating the discussion; for it has been established for you by the various previous proofs the existence of God Almighty, and that is the evidence for His being described with this attribute, for it, as we said, is nothing other than His essence, may He be glorified and exalted.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to the attributes of God. It begins by affirming that God possesses all perfect attributes and is free from all imperfections, because His divinity logically requires absolute perfection. Then it states that we must detail the most important of these attributes, which are found in the Quran and can be known through definitive proofs. These attributes are summarized into twenty principal attributes, which are divided into four categories: the attribute of Self (al-ṣifa al-nafsiyya), negative attributes (al-ṣifāt al-salbiyya), attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-maʿānī), and the attributes entailed by meanings (al-ṣifāt al-maʿnawiyya). The author then explains the first category: the attribute of Self. This is a positive attribute that refers to the essence itself without implying anything additional, like when we say a substance is a substance or a thing exists. There is only one attribute of Self, which is existence (al-wujūd). The author notes that the existence of God has already been proven by previous arguments, and that this existence is not something separate from His essence—it is identical to His being.

Key Terms
صفات الكمال
صفات النقصان
الصفة النفسية
الوجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The attribute of Self (existence) is a separate quality added to God's essence.
Correction: The passage explains that the attribute of Self is a positive attribute that indicates the essence without an additional meaning; existence is not separate from God but identical to His essence.

Checkpoint
What is the attribute of Self (al-ṣifa al-nafsiyya)?
A) A negative attribute that denies imperfection.
B) A positive attribute that indicates the essence without additional meaning.
C) An attribute of meaning that inheres in the essence.
D) An attribute that describes God's actions.

Key Takeaway
The attribute of Self is existence, which is not a separate attribute but identical to God's essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever treated God's existence as merely a fact or a doctrine, rather than the very core of who He is? How would your prayers change if you truly believed that His existence is not a quality He possesses but what He is?
?
If God's perfection is absolute and necessary, what does that reveal about your own attempts to 'perfect' yourself apart from Him? In what area of your life are you still acting as if your existence and worth depend on your own efforts, rather than on the One whose essence is existence itself?
?
The passage says God's divinity necessitates absolute perfection. Does your worship reflect a deep, unwavering conviction that God is perfect and needs nothing from you? Or do you sometimes worship with a sense of bargaining, as if your actions add to His glory? What would it take for you to let go of that mentality today?

Divine Attributes

Negative Attributes and Their Five Comprehensive Categories
Buti defines negative attributes and states they reduce to five principal ones.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of negative attributes (al-sifat al-salbiyya) and why Islamic theology reduces them to five comprehensive ones.

Core Idea
Negative attributes are not about what God is, but about what God is not.

Buti begins by explaining that negative attributes negate whatever is unbefitting to God. While deficiencies are countless, the theologians have identified five principal categories. This lesson introduces that foundational concept.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of negative attributes
Read the first sentence carefully: negative attributes signify the absence of something unbefitting. Understand the concept.
2
Understand why five suffice
The passage says there are five 'mothers' that cover all particulars. Reflect on how a few categories can encompass many negations.
3
Prepare for the five attributes
The passage ends by announcing the five attributes. This sets up the next lesson where the first one is explained.
The next lesson will detail the first attribute, oneness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ب - الصفات السلبية وهي كل صفة مدلولها عدم أمر لا يليق بالله سبحانه ، وهذه الصفات كثيرة الجزئيات لأن كل نقص إنما يُنفى بعكسه ، والنقائص كثيرة الأشكال والأنواع إلا أن هنالك خمس صفات هي أمهات الصفات السلبية كلها ، فيكتفى بها عما سواها من الجزئيات الكثيرة ولنبدأ بذكر هذه الصفات الخمس وشرحها من ١ - ( الوحدانية ( ومعناها سلب تصور الكمية في ذاته وصفاته سبحانه وتعالى : سواء الكمية المتصلة والكمية المنفصلة أي فهو سبحانه وتعالى ليس مركباً أجزاء ولا مكوناً من جزئيات ، وكذلك صفاته .. فليس له سبحانه وتعالى مثلاً علمان أو قدرتان ، بحيث تتم كل واحدة منها الأخرى . فهذا هو نفي الأجزاء عنها . وليس لغيره سبحانه وتعالى علم كعلمه ، أو قدرة كقدرته ، فهذا هو نفي الجزئيات عنها . والجزء من الشيء ، ما يتركب ذلك الشيء منه ومن غيره ، بحيث لا يصدق اسم ذلك الشيء عليه وحده حتى تتكامل معه بقية أجزائه الأخرى ، مثل الجدار من الغرفة والغلاف من الكتاب واليد من الإنسان . ويطلق على مجموع الأجزاء بعد تناسقها وتمامها اسم الكل ، فالغرفة كل والجدار الواحد جزء منه والجزئي هو ما يندرج تحت الجنس أو النوع من الأعداد والأفراد ، بحيث يصح إطلاق ذلك الجنس أو النوع على كل فرد من أفراده على حدة ، مثل الإنسان ، فهو اسم لنوع من الحيوان يندرج تحته أعداد وأفراد كثيرة . ومن المعلوم أن اسم الإنسان كما يطلق على النوع في جملته ، يطلق أيضاً على الفرد الواحد تحته ، فنقول عن فلان من الناس : إنسان ، ويطلق على النوع أو الجنس المندرج الشامل لكل الأفراد اسم الكلي وبهذا نعلم أن الجزء يقابله الكل ، والجزئي يقابله الكلي فالمقصود بوحدانية الله أن تعلم بأنه سبحانه وتعالى ليس كلاً مركباً من أجزاء ولا كلياً مكوناً من جزئيات . والدليل الجامع على ذلك قوله تعالى : ﴿ قُلْ هُوَ اللهُ أَحَدٌ ) فقد نفت الآية ، بإسناد صفة الوحدانية إليه ، كلاً من صفة الكل والكلية عنه
B - The negative attributes: they are every attribute whose signification is the absence of something unbefitting to God, exalted. These attributes have many particulars because every deficiency is negated by its opposite, and deficiencies are many in forms and types, but there are five attributes that are the mothers of all negative attributes, so they suffice instead of the many particulars. Let us begin to mention these five attributes and explain them. 1 - Al-Wahdaniyya (Oneness): its meaning is the negation of the conception of quantity regarding His essence and attributes, exalted: both continuous quantity and discrete quantity, i.e., He, exalted, is not composed of parts nor made up of particulars, and likewise His attributes. So He does not have, for example, two knowledges or two powers such that each one completes the other. This is the negation of parts from them. And no other besides Him has knowledge like His knowledge or power like His power. This is the negation of particulars from them. The part (al-juz') of something is that from which that thing is composed along with other things, such that the name of that thing is not applied to it alone until the rest of its parts are completed with it, like the wall of the room, the cover of the book, and the hand of the human. The sum of the parts after their coordination and completion is called the whole (al-kull). So the room is a whole and the single wall is a part of it. The particular (al-juz'i) is that which falls under the genus or species of numbers and individuals, such that it is correct to apply that genus or species to each individual of its individuals separately, like 'human': it is the name of a species of animal under which many numbers and individuals fall. It is known that the name 'human' as applied to the species in its entirety is also applied to the single individual under it. So we say about a certain person: 'human'. The genus or species that encompasses all individuals is called the universal (al-kulli). By this we know that the part is contrasted with the whole, and the particular is contrasted with the universal. What is intended by God's oneness is that you know that He, exalted, is neither a whole composed of parts nor a universal made up of particulars. The comprehensive proof of that is His saying: 'Say: He is Allah, the One' (Qul huwa Allahu ahad). The verse, by attributing the attribute of oneness to Him, negates both the attribute of whole and universality from Him.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage defines the category of negative attributes (al-sifat al-salbiyya) and then focuses on the first of the five principal ones: al-wahdaniyya (oneness). It begins by explaining that negative attributes are those that negate anything unbefitting to God. Among them, five are comprehensive. Then it defines oneness as negation of quantity (kamiyya) in God's essence and attributes, both continuous (composition) and discrete (multiplicity). The explanation clarifies that God is not composed of parts (like a whole) nor made up of individuals (like a universal). It then defines the terms 'part' (juz') and 'whole' (kull), and 'particular' (juz'i) and 'universal' (kulli), illustrating with examples. Finally, it gives the Qur'anic proof from Surah al-Ikhlas that negates both composition and universality from God.

Key Terms
الصفات السلبية
الجزئيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Negative attributes are just saying 'God is not bad' or are unnecessary.
Correction: Negative attributes are essential to preserve God's transcendence; they negate specific imperfections and form a structured system in theology.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are only five negative attributes needed?
A) Because there are only five deficiencies.
B) Because they are the mothers that cover all particular negations.
C) Because the Quran only mentions five.
D) Because the Prophet specified five.

Key Takeaway
Negative attributes are not arbitrary; they are rooted in five comprehensive categories that guard God's transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you contemplate God's attributes, do you instinctively focus on what He is not rather than what He is? How might this emphasis shape the way you approach Him in prayer and trust? This week, try to consciously affirm one positive attribute of God each time you negate a deficiency.
?
The lesson says that negative attributes guard God's transcendence. Is there an attribute of God—like mercy, power, or justice—that you find yourself limiting by human standards? How can the way you negate deficiencies from God's attributes free you to rely on Him more fully?
?
You believe that God is free from all deficiencies. But are there areas in your own life where you stubbornly cling to a deficiency—like pride, impatience, or ingratitude—that contradicts the perfection you ascribe to God? What step can you take today to remove that contradiction?

The Meaning and Proof of Divine Oneness (Al-Wahdaniyya)
Buti defines oneness as negation of quantity, explains part/whole and particular/universal distinctions, and gives Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical meaning of God's oneness as negation of composition and multiplicity, and the Quranic proof from Surah al-Ikhlas.

Core Idea
God's oneness means He is not a whole made of parts nor a universal made of individuals.

This lesson unpacks the first negative attribute: al-wahdaniyya (oneness). It goes beyond the common understanding of 'no other gods' to explain that God cannot be composed of parts or belong to a category of beings. The passage uses logical terms like part, whole, particular, and universal, and concludes with the ultimate proof from the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of oneness
Read the definition: oneness negates quantity in God's essence and attributes, both continuous and discrete.
2
Distinguish between parts and particulars
The passage distinguishes between composition (parts making a whole) and multiplicity (individuals under a universal). Study the examples: wall of a room, hand of a human, etc.
Parts are components of a whole; particulars are instances of a universal category.
3
Understand the proof from Surah al-Ikhlas
The verse 'Qul huwa Allahu ahad' negates both whole and universality. Reflect on how the verse implies negation of composition and multiplicity.

B - The negative attributes: they are every attribute whose signification is the absence of something unbefitting to God, exalted. These attributes have many particulars because every deficiency is negated by its opposite, and deficiencies are many in forms and types, but there are five attributes that are the mothers of all negative attributes, so they suffice instead of the many particulars. Let us begin to mention these five attributes and explain them. 1 - Al-Wahdaniyya (Oneness): its meaning is the negation of the conception of quantity regarding His essence and attributes, exalted: both continuous quantity and discrete quantity, i.e., He, exalted, is not composed of parts nor made up of particulars, and likewise His attributes. So He does not have, for example, two knowledges or two powers such that each one completes the other. This is the negation of parts from them. And no other besides Him has knowledge like His knowledge or power like His power. This is the negation of particulars from them. The part (al-juz') of something is that from which that thing is composed along with other things, such that the name of that thing is not applied to it alone until the rest of its parts are completed with it, like the wall of the room, the cover of the book, and the hand of the human. The sum of the parts after their coordination and completion is called the whole (al-kull). So the room is a whole and the single wall is a part of it. The particular (al-juz'i) is that which falls under the genus or species of numbers and individuals, such that it is correct to apply that genus or species to each individual of its individuals separately, like 'human': it is the name of a species of animal under which many numbers and individuals fall. It is known that the name 'human' as applied to the species in its entirety is also applied to the single individual under it. So we say about a certain person: 'human'. The genus or species that encompasses all individuals is called the universal (al-kulli). By this we know that the part is contrasted with the whole, and the particular is contrasted with the universal. What is intended by God's oneness is that you know that He, exalted, is neither a whole composed of parts nor a universal made up of particulars. The comprehensive proof of that is His saying: 'Say: He is Allah, the One' (Qul huwa Allahu ahad). The verse, by attributing the attribute of oneness to Him, negates both the attribute of whole and universality from Him.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage defines the category of negative attributes (al-sifat al-salbiyya) and then focuses on the first of the five principal ones: al-wahdaniyya (oneness). It begins by explaining that negative attributes are those that negate anything unbefitting to God. Among them, five are comprehensive. Then it defines oneness as negation of quantity (kamiyya) in God's essence and attributes, both continuous (composition) and discrete (multiplicity). The explanation clarifies that God is not composed of parts (like a whole) nor made up of individuals (like a universal). It then defines the terms 'part' (juz') and 'whole' (kull), and 'particular' (juz'i) and 'universal' (kulli), illustrating with examples. Finally, it gives the Qur'anic proof from Surah al-Ikhlas that negates both composition and universality from God.

Correction: Oneness also negates any composition in God's essence or attributes and any multiplicity or instances of His attributes.

The Attribute of Qidam (Eternality) and Its Proof
Buti defines qidam and provides its rational proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of qidam as the absence of a beginning for God, the combined scriptural and rational proof for this attribute, and why the question 'Who created God?' arises from a failure to grasp qidam.

Core Idea
If God had a beginning, He would need a creator or lead to infinite regress; therefore He must be eternal.

Buti opens by defining qidam—meaning God has no beginning. He then presents a proof from the Quran and a rational dilemma: if God were preceded by non-existence, He would require an external creator, which either leads to another eternal being or to an impossible infinite regress. He prepares the ground for answering a common objection by noting that the human mind struggles to conceive of something eternal because all perceptions come through the senses.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of qidam
The passage begins with a clear definition: qidam means that God has no beginning. Notice the Arabic term and its articulation.
2
Examine the scriptural proof
Buti cites Quran 57:3, where God is called 'the First.' This establishes qidam from revelation.
Scripture supports reason.
3
Follow the rational dilemma
The passage presents a conditional: if God were preceded by non-existence, He would need a creator. Either that creator is Himself (making Him eternal) or it leads to infinite regress (tasalsul), which is invalid. Therefore God must be eternal.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
4
Understand the source of the objection
Buti explains that the question 'Who created God?' arises because the mind cannot conceive of something without a beginning. The answer begins by noting that all human perceptions come through the senses, so the mind cannot directly grasp qidam.
The passage is cut off before the full answer.

2 - al-Qidam (Eternality): and its meaning is that He, glorified and exalted, has no beginning. The proof for the establishment of this attribute for Him is His saying: 'He is the First and the Last, the Manifest and the Hidden' (Quran 57:3). And that if He were preceded by non-existence, there would necessarily be an influencer in bringing Him into existence, and it is impossible that along with that He be a god. Then, either the god must be the one preceding Him and bringing Him into existence, so He would be the Eternal – and this is the intended clarification – or that preceding one is also preceded by non-existence and an existent affected him so brought him into existence, and so on, necessitating the assumption of infinite regress (tasalsul), which is invalid by the scientific proof we have already presented and clarified. So all existents must necessarily be dependent in their existence upon a self-necessary existence (dhat wajib al-wujud); and this self cannot be necessary of existence unless it is effective upon others not affected by others. And that necessitates that it be qualified with qidam (eternality). This is a clear scientific proof that the intellect cannot dispute; it must affirm it. But after that, the intellect may be incapable of conceiving this qidam and digesting it analytically and adaptively. For that reason, you see some superficial people harboring in themselves this question: 'Who created God?' The source of this question, as I told you, is that the imagination of the questioner cannot digest the image of qidam and its meaning relative to the essence of God. And since man is eager to conceive and touch every reality presented to him, he does not cease thinking about that question. But the problem is removed by clarifying the following truth: All human perceptions are only the offspring of his concepts, and concepts are gathered in the mind through the windows of the five senses. Commentary
This passage deals with the divine attribute of qidam (eternality, having no beginning). The author first defines qidam as the absence of a beginning for God. The proof is both scriptural (Quran 57:3, where God is called 'the First') and rational. The rational argument proceeds by dilemma: if God had a beginning, He would need a creator. That creator must either be God Himself (making Him eternal) or lead to infinite regress, which is invalid. Therefore, all existence depends on a self-necessary being (wajib al-wujud) that is unaffected. That being must possess qidam. The author emphasizes that this is a clear proof, but the human mind may still struggle to grasp how something can be eternal. That leads to the common question 'Who created God?' The source of this question is the mind's inability to conceive of an eternal thing, as the mind works through sensory concepts. The answer begins (though cut off) by explaining that all perceptions come through the senses, so the mind cannot directly conceive of something outside its scope. The passage is incomplete but establishes the proof and the nature of the doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is valid to ask 'Who created God?' because everything must have a cause.
Correction: God is eternal (qidam), meaning He has no beginning; the principle of causality applies only to contingent beings.

Proof of God's Attribute of Qidam (Eternal Pre-existence)
Defines qidam and presents a proof from Quran and logical reasoning against infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of qidam (eternal pre-existence) and the rational proof that establishes it for Allah, grounded in both revelation and logical necessity.

Core Idea
If God had a beginning, He would need a creator—leading to an infinite regress or another god, both impossible.

Before we can speak of God's attributes, we must establish that He is eternal—without beginning. This lesson presents a combined scriptural and rational argument for the attribute of qidam. The proof uses a conditional chain to show that any being that is not eternal would require an external cause, ultimately grounding all existence in a self-sufficient, uncaused essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Note the flow: definition → Quranic evidence → logical argument.
The passage is rich in reasoning; take time to follow each conditional.
2
Understand the meaning of qidam
Identify the definition given: 'having no beginning.' Contrast this with temporal existence.
This is the foundational attribute for all others.
3
Analyze the logical proof
Trace the conditional: if God were preceded by non-existence, He would need a creator. This leads to two options: another god (contradiction) or infinite regress (absurd). Both are impossible, so God must be eternal.
The argument depends on rejecting infinite regress, which the author says was already disproven.
4
Connect to the Necessary Existent
The proof concludes that all existents depend on a self-existent essence (wajib al-wujud) that is uncaused and uncausing—this is the eternal God.
This links qidam to the broader proof for God's existence.

2. Al-Qidam (Eternal Pre-existence): Its meaning is that He, glorified and exalted, has no beginning. The proof of the affirmation of this attribute for Him, glorified and exalted, is His saying, the Exalted: 'He is the First and the Last, the Apparent and the Hidden' [Surah al-Hadid: 3]. And that if He were preceded by non-existence, then there would necessarily be an effecter in bringing Him into existence, and it would be impossible for Him to be a god with that. Therefore, necessarily, all existents must be dependent in their existence upon an essence that is necessarily existent (wajib al-wujud); and this essence is not necessarily existent unless it is effecting others and not affected by others. And that requires that it be described with eternal pre-existence (qidam). This is a clear scientific proof that the intellect cannot dispute; it must affirm it.

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of qidam (eternal pre-existence) as having no beginning and provides a proof for it. The author begins with the Quranic verse 'He is the First...' as scriptural evidence. Then he presents a logical argument: if God were preceded by non-existence, He would need a creator, which would either be another god (leading to an impossibility—that god would be the eternal one) or lead to infinite regress (tasalsul). Infinite regress is rejected by a prior scientific proof. Therefore, existence must be grounded in a self-existent, uncaused essence (wajib al-wujud) that is not affected by others—this essence is eternal. The argument is presented as irrefutable by reason.

What would it look like for you to embrace the certainty that Allah is the First and that everything depends on Him?

Answering 'Who Created God?'
Explains the psychological source of the question and refutes it by appealing to human cognitive limits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the question 'Who created God?' arises from a limitation of human imagination and how rational proof overcomes that limitation.

Core Idea
Inability to imagine something does not mean it is impossible.

In this passage, the author addresses a common and persistent objection to belief in God's eternity. He does not merely dismiss it but traces it to a psychological and epistemological root: the human tendency to rely on sensory experience for understanding. By the end, you will see why this question is not a genuine intellectual challenge but a symptom of limited imagination.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the translation. Note the author's tone and the logical progression.
The passage builds step by step from the question to the cure.
2
Identify the source of the question
Locate where the author states that the question arises from an inability to conceive qidam (eternity without beginning). Understand that the imagination cannot 'digest' this concept.
This is the psychological root.
3
Understand the epistemological principle
The author explains that all human concepts come through the five senses. Abstract ideas without sensory models are impossible to imagine. This is key to understanding why qidam is hard to grasp.
Examples of mercy and justice show what is easy; spaceless/timeless and no-beginning show what is hard.
4
Grasp the philosophical maxim and conclusion
The author cites the maxim 'lack of finding does not necessitate non-existence'. Realize that the mind's limitation does not mean God's eternity is false; rational proof (from earlier) suffices for certainty.
The lesson ends with a humbling reminder of human cognitive limits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولكن العقل بعد ذلك قد يعجز عن تصور هذا القدم وهضمه تحليلاً وتكييفاً . ومن أجل ذلك ترى بعض السطحيين يحوك في نفوسهم هذا التساؤل : من الذي خلق الله ؟ . ومصدر هذا التساؤل ، كما قلت لك ، أن خيال السائل لا يهضم صورة القدم ومعناه بالنسبة لذات الله تعالى ، ولما كان الإنسان متطلعاً إلى تصور ولمس كل حقيقة تعرض عليه فإنه لا يفتأ يفكر في ذلك السؤال ولكن الإشكال يزول بإيضاح هذه الحقيقة التالية : إن جميع مدارك الإنسان إنما هو وليد تصوراته ، والتصورات إنما تتجمع في الذهن عن طريق نوافذ الحواس الخمس . وهذا يعني أن الإنسان لا يعقل من المجردات إلا ماكان له مقاييس ونماذج حسية في ذهنه ، فما لم يسبق له في ذهنه أي نموذج أو مقياس فإن من المحال بالنسبة إليه أن يتصوره ويدركه . وعلى هذا القياس فإن من السهل عليك أن تفهم صفة الرحمة في ذات الله تعالى لأنك تحتفظ في ذهنك بتصورات لمعانيها وآثارها ؛ ومن السهل عليك أن تتصور له صفة العدل والجلال والإكرام ، وأنه شديد العقاب ، لأنها كلها تعود إلى معان توجد في ذهنك صور لها ، وإن كانت هذه الصفات مختلفة في ذاته تعالى عنها في ذوات المخلوقين . فإذا قيل لك إنه لا يحده مكان ولا زمان ، فهذا ما لا تدركه ، لأنك لا تحتفظ في ذهنك بأي معنى أو صورة لهذه الصفة أنها صفة خاصة بذاته تعالى . وكذلك إذا قيل لك إنه سبحانه وتعالى قديم لا أول ، فأنت تذهب لتتخيل صورة عدم الأولية ، فلا تستطيع أن تتخيل أو تتصور له بسبب ذلك . إذ إنه معنى طارئ على مخيلتك لم تسبقه رؤية الحقيقته أو ممارسة له بذاته ولذلك فلا مطمع لأن يهضم خيالك أو تصورك هذا المعنى . غير أن من السهل عليك جداً ، وقد أدركت هذه الحقيقة وآمنت بها عن طريق البرهان العلمي الذي ذكرناه ، أن تتيقنها وتعتقد بها اعتقاداً جازماً دون أن تنتظر إمكان تصورك لها ، لأن من السهل عليك أن تفهم أن عقلك لم يستوعب جميع حقائق الوجود ، وأن فكرك لم يسجل جميع صوره وأشكاله . وفي ذلك يقول الفلاسفة وعامة العقلاء والباحثين : ( عدم الوجدان للشيء لا يستلزم عدم وجوده في الواقع ) . فالعقل إنما يدرك بواسطة نوافذ الحواس الخمس والحواس الخمس تحس بقدر محدود وإلى مسافة محدودة فهل هذا يعني أن ما وراء هذا المحدود هو اللاشيء ؟! إن الاستمرار اللانهائي لا يدرك ، وليس ذلك إلا لأن الطاقة الفكرية في الإنسان محدودة ومتناهية
But the intellect after that may be unable to conceive of this qidam and digest it analytically and qualitatively. Because of that, you see some superficial people harboring this question in themselves: Who created God? The source of this question, as I told you, is that the imagination of the questioner cannot digest the image of qidam and its meaning with respect to the essence of God Almighty. And since man is eager to conceive and touch every truth presented to him, he does not stop thinking about that question. But the problem is removed by clarifying the following fact: All of man's perceptions are only the offspring of his concepts, and concepts are only gathered in the mind through the windows of the five senses. This means that man only comprehends from abstractions that which has sensory measures and models in his mind. So whatever has not been preceded in his mind by any model or measure, it is impossible for him to conceive it and perceive it. On this basis, it is easy for you to understand the attribute of mercy in the essence of God Almighty because you retain in your mind concepts of its meanings and effects; and it is easy for you to conceive for Him the attribute of justice, majesty, generosity, and that He is severe in punishment, because all of them refer to meanings for which you have images in your mind, even though these attributes are different in His essence, Exalted is He, from what they are in the essences of creatures. So if it is said to you that He is not limited by place or time, then this is something you do not perceive, because you do not retain in your mind any meaning or image for this attribute, as it is a specific attribute of His essence. Likewise, if it is said to you that He, glorified and exalted, is eternal with no beginning, you go to imagine an image of non-beginning-ness, but you cannot imagine or conceive it because of that. Because it is a meaning incidental to your imagination that has not been preceded by seeing its reality or experiencing it itself. Therefore, there is no hope for your imagination or concept to digest this meaning. However, it is very easy for you, having grasped this truth and believed in it through the scientific proof we mentioned, to be certain of it and believe in it with firm conviction without waiting for the possibility of conceiving it, because it is easy for you to understand that your mind has not encompassed all the realities of existence, and that your thought has not recorded all its images and forms. And on that, the philosophers and all reasonable people and researchers say: 'The lack of finding something does not necessitate its non-existence in reality.' For the intellect only perceives through the windows of the five senses, and the five senses sense to a limited extent and to a limited distance. Does this mean that what is beyond this limited is nothing? Continuous infinity cannot be perceived, and that is only because the intellectual energy in man is limited and finite.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage addresses the common objection 'Who created God?' The author explains that the question arises from an inability to conceive of qidam. He then provides an epistemological argument: human concepts derive from sensory experience; abstract ideas like 'no beginning' have no sensory model, so the mind struggles to imagine them. However, this does not invalidate their reality. The author illustrates with examples: attributes like mercy and justice have sensory correlates (effects in the world), so they are easier to conceive, but attributes like being beyond space and time or having no beginning lack such correlates. Nonetheless, once the rational proof (presented earlier) establishes the reality of qidam, one should affirm it with certainty despite the inability to imagine it. The author cites the philosophical maxim 'lack of finding does not necessitate non-existence' and concludes by emphasizing the limited nature of human cognition.

Key Terms
قدم (qidam)
عدم الوجدان (adam al-wijdan)
الحواس الخمس (al-hawass al-khams)
التصور (tasawwur)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If I cannot imagine something (like God's eternity), then it cannot exist.
Correction: The passage explains that imagination is limited to sensory experience; lack of ability to conceive does not mean non-existence. Rational proof is the proper criterion.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why do some people ask 'Who created God?'
A) Because they reject the rational proof

C) Because they are atheists
D) Because they misunderstand the Quran

Key Takeaway
The question 'Who created God?' stems from a limited human imagination; rational proof, not imagination, is the basis for certainty about God's eternity.

The Meaning and Textual Proof of God's Permanence
Buti defines al-baqa' and cites the Qur'anic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the divine attribute of permanence (al-baqa') and its textual proof from the Qur'an.

Core Idea
Permanence means that non-existence can never touch God.

In this lesson, we explore the attribute of permanence (al-baqa'), which is the opposite of the possibility of ceasing to exist. The author defines it clearly and then provides a scriptural proof from the same verse that establishes God's eternality. This shows that God is not only without beginning but also without end.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Read the first part: 'Permanence: its meaning is the impossibility of non-existence attaching to His essence.' Understand that this attribute is about God being everlasting.
2
Note the transmitted proof
The verse 'He is the First and the Last' serves as proof for both eternality (al-qidam) and permanence. See how the same verse covers both attributes.
3
Reflect on the relationship
Think about why the same verse proves both attributes: just as there is no beginning for God, there is no end.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣ - ( البقاء ( ومعناه امتناع لحوق العدم بذاته سبحانه وتعالى ، ودليله النقلي الآية ذاتها التي هي دليل القدم ، وهي قوله تعالى : هوَ الأَوَّلُ والآخِرُ والظَّاهِرُ والباطنُ ﴾ [الحديد: ٣] ويقال في دليله العقلي ما قلناه في دليل القدم . إذ كما لا يتصور وجود مؤثر في واجب الوجود بالإيجاد فلا يتصور وجود مؤثر فيه بالإعدام ، وإلا لم يكن واجب الوجود . كما أنه يمكن فهم هذه الصفة بالطريقة ذاتها التي نفهم بها صفة القدم ، إذ كلا الصفتين لا مقياس في الخيال لها ، وإن كان في العقل دليل على ثبوتها . فمن المستحيل أن يستطيع الخيال تصورهما وفهم حقيقتها وإن كان العقل يجزم في الوقت نفسه بثبوتها . وهكذا تعلم أن عدم قدرة العقل على تصور الشيء ، ليس دليلاً على عدمه البتة كما هو واضح معلوم
3. Permanence (al-baqa'): Its meaning is the impossibility of non-existence attaching to His essence, glorified and exalted be He. Its transmitted proof is the same verse that is the proof of eternality, namely His saying: 'He is the First and the Last, the Manifest and the Hidden' (Qur'an 57:3). And as for its rational proof, it is what we said in the proof of eternality. For just as it is inconceivable that there exists an effecting agent upon the Necessary Existence with regard to bringing into existence, so it is inconceivable that there exists an effecting agent upon it with regard to annihilating it; otherwise, it would not be the Necessary Existence. Also, it is possible to understand this attribute in the same way we understand the attribute of eternality, for both attributes have no measure in the imagination, even though there is in the mind a proof of their establishment. So it is impossible for the imagination to conceive them and understand their reality, even though the mind simultaneously affirms their establishment. Thus you learn that the mind's inability to conceive something is absolutely not a proof of its non-existence, as is clear and known.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the divine attribute of permanence (al-baqa'). The author begins by defining it as the impossibility of non-existence attaching to God's essence. He then gives two proofs: first, the transmitted proof from the Qur'anic verse, which is the same verse used for eternality, indicating that God is the Last as He is the First. Second, the rational proof: just as it is inconceivable that any external agent could bring the Necessary Existence into being, so it is inconceivable that any external agent could annihilate it, because if it were possible for something to affect its non-existence, it would not be necessary in its existence. He then notes that this attribute, like eternality, cannot be imagined, but reason affirms it. He concludes by reiterating the earlier principle: the mind's inability to conceive something does not prove its non-existence.

Key Terms
البقاء
امتناع لحوق العدم
القدم
الأَوَّلُ
الآخِرُ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which Qur'anic verse is used as the transmitted proof for the attribute of permanence?
A) The verse of the Throne
B) 'He is the First and the Last' (57:3)
C) 'Everything will perish save His Face'
D) 'And He is with you wherever you are'

Key Takeaway
The attribute of permanence means God cannot cease to exist, proven by the Qur'anic verse that declares He is the Last.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

?
Because non-existence can never touch God, He is the only unshakable reality. When you face a fear of losing something or someone, how does knowing that God's permanence is absolute affect your trust in Him? What will you do the next time that fear arises?

Rational Proof for Permanence and the Limits of Imagination
Buti presents the rational proof for permanence and clarifies the role of reason vs imagination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument for God's permanence and why the imagination's inability to grasp it does not negate its reality.

Core Idea
Just as no one can bring God into existence, no one can annihilate Him.

This lesson continues from the textual proof and provides a rational argument for God's permanence. The author draws a parallel between creation and annihilation: if no external agent can bring the Necessary Existence into being, similarly no agent can cause its non-existence. He also addresses a potential objection: that we cannot imagine permanence, but rational proof suffices.

Guided Path
1
Understand the rational proof
Read the rational proof: just as there is no agent to bring God into existence, there is no agent to annihilate Him, because He is the Necessary Existence. If something could annihilate Him, He would not be necessary.
Notice the logical parallel.
2
Compare with eternality
The author says permanence is understood the same way as eternality: both have no measure in imagination but are affirmed by reason.
3
Grasp the principle
The lesson concludes with a general principle: the mind's inability to conceive something does not prove it doesn't exist. This is crucial for many theological concepts.

The Divine Attribute of Self-Subsistence (al-Qiyam bi al-Dhat)
Buti defines al-qiyam bi al-dhat, provides proofs, and answers an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of God's self-subsistence, its proofs, and how to answer the objection that every existent must be located in a place.

Core Idea
God needs nothing and everything needs Him.

One of the essential divine attributes is self-subsistence (al-qiyam bi al-dhat), meaning that God is independent of any creator or substrate. Buti here defines this attribute, provides both rational and scriptural proofs, and then addresses a common objection: how can God exist without being in a place? He shows that our knowledge of place from contingent things does not apply to God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the translation. Notice how Buti defines the attribute, gives the proof from the Qur'an, and then handles the objection.
The Arabic text ends abruptly, but the argument is complete enough.
2
Understand the definition
Focus on the definition: God does not need a creator or a substrate. He is self-sufficient.
The term 'al-Samad' from Surah al-Ikhlas captures this.
3
Examine the proofs
There is a scriptural proof (Qur'an 112:2) and a rational proof: since God is Necessary Existence and eternal, He cannot be affected or need anything.
4
Study the objection and answer
The objection says every existent we know is in a place. The answer is that this induction applies only to contingent things, not to God.
This shows the limits of analogical reasoning about God.
5
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this attribute is fundamental for tawheed. It eliminates any notion of God being dependent or limited.
Connect to the concept of 'samadiyyah'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤ - ( القيام بالذات ( أي إنه تعالى غير مفتقر إلى موجد يوجده ولا إلى محل يقوم به . فقد كان الله تعالى قبل وجود أي شيء وقبل وجود الزمان ( أي الأفلاك التي تحد سير الوقت ) والمكان . والدليل على ثبوت هذه الصفة الله تعالى بالإضافة إلى دليل العقل الواضح قوله تعالى : و اللهُ الصَّمَد أي الذي لا يحتاج إلى شيء ويحتاج إليه كل شيء . واعلم أنه لا مجال لتوقف العقل في إثبات هذه الصفة الله تعالى ، بعد معرفة أنه واجب الوجود وأنه قديم لا يتأثر بشيء ويتأثر به كل شيء .. فإن قلت : كيف أفهم أنه لا مكان لله ، والذي أعلمه أنه ما من موجود ، إلا وهو متحيز في مكان ما ؟ فالجواب أن علمك هذا إنما استقيته من استقراء حالات الأجسام والحوادث . والصفات المتلبسة بالأشياء الممكنة والحادثة لا يجب تلبسها
4. Self-subsistence (al-qiyam bi al-dhat): That is, He, exalted be He, is not in need of a creator to create Him nor of a substrate in which to subsist. For God existed before the existence of anything and before the existence of time (i.e., the spheres that define the passage of time) and place. The proof for the establishment of this attribute of God, in addition to the clear rational proof, is His saying: 'And God is al-Samad' (Qur'an 112:2), i.e. the one who needs nothing and everything needs Him. Know that there is no room for the mind to hesitate in affirming this attribute of God, after knowing that He is the Necessary Existence and that He is eternal, not affected by anything while everything is affected by Him. If you say: How can I understand that God has no place, while I know that there is no existent except that it is located in some place? The answer is that this knowledge of yours is only derived from induction of the states of bodies and events. The attributes that are attached to possible and contingent things are not necessarily attached to [God].
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the divine attribute of self-subsistence (al-qiyam bi al-dhat), along with an objection and answer. The author defines it as God not needing a creator or a substrate. He states that God existed before all things, time, and place. The transmitted proof is the Qur'anic verse 'God is al-Samad', meaning He needs nothing and everything needs Him. The rational proof is that since God is the Necessary Existence and eternal, He is not affected by anything, whereas everything is affected by Him; thus He has no need for a place. Then an objection is raised: 'How can I understand that God has no place, while I know that every existent is located in a place?' The answer is that this knowledge is derived from observing bodies and events, which are contingent. The attributes that apply to contingent things do not necessarily apply to God. The text cuts off at this point, but the argument is clear: God's self-subsistence means He is not subject to the limitations of spatiality that apply to created beings.

Key Terms
القيام بالذات
الصمد
واجب الوجود
المكان
المتحيز
الأجسام
الحوادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Every existent, including God, must be located in a place.
Correction: Our knowledge that existents are located in places comes from observing contingent bodies and events. God, as Necessary Existence, is not subject to the attributes of contingent things, so He does not require a place.

Checkpoint
What is the answer Buti gives to the objection that every existent is located in a place?
A) God has a place but it is unknown.
B) The attributes of contingent things do not necessarily apply to God.
C) The mind cannot answer this objection.
D) God is in every place.

Key Takeaway
God's self-subsistence means He is completely independent of any creator, substrate, time, or place—a truth established by both scripture and reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as if God is al-Samad—the One you need for everything? In what area of your life are you still relying on yourself or others, ignoring your absolute need for Him?
?
When you feel lost or without a 'place' in life, do you remember that God is beyond all places, yet closer to you than your jugular vein? How does this change your sense of belonging?
?
The rational proof shows that God is not affected by anything. Is there a fear or worry that implies God could be affected by your mistakes or circumstances? How can you realign your understanding to His self-subsistence?

The Attribute of al-Baqā' (Eternal Duration)
Defines al-baqā' with transmitted and rational proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of the divine attribute al-baqā', its transmitted and rational proofs, and the principle that inability to imagine something does not negate its reality.

Core Idea
Eternal duration means no non-existence can ever befall Allah, and reason proves it.

This lesson introduces the third divine attribute discussed by Sanusi: al-baqā', or eternal duration. After establishing the principle that the mind's inability to picture something does not make it impossible, the passage defines al-baqā' and provides both scriptural and rational proofs. You will see how the same Quranic verse used for al-qidam also supports al-baqā', and how rational reasoning parallels that of eternal past existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then its translation. Let the author's flow sink in before interpreting.
Notice the general principle at the beginning about imagination and intellect.
2
Identify the opening principle
The passage starts by stating that the intellect's inability to conceive something does not mean it's impossible. This principle is crucial for understanding attributes that are beyond imagination.
3
Find the definition and proofs
The attribute is defined as the impossibility of non-existence attaching to Allah's essence. Then two proofs are given: a transmitted proof (the same verse as for al-qidam) and a rational proof (no cause can annihilate the Necessary Existent).
The rational proof is parallel to that of al-qidam.
4
Understand the conclusion
The passage concludes that both al-qidam and al-baqā' are affirmed by reason but beyond imagination. This reinforces the initial principle: inability to imagine is not evidence of non-existence.
This is a key takeaway for kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولكن ذلك لا يعني أن العقل يجزم باستحالته، فرب أمر يدرك العقل إمكانه أو وجوده وهو في الوقت نفسه يعجز عن تصوره وإدراك كنهه. ٣ - ( البقاء ( ومعناه امتناع لحوق العدم بذاته سبحانه وتعالى، ودليـله النقلي الآية ذاتها التي هي دليل القدم، وهي قوله تعالى: ﴿ هوَ الأَوَّلُ والآخِرُ والظَّاهِرُ والباطنُ ﴾ [الحديد: ٣] ويقال في دليلـه العقلي ما قلناه في دليل القدم. إذ كما لا يتصور وجود مؤثر في واجب الوجود بالإيجاد فلا يتصور وجود مؤثر فيه بالإعدام، وإلا لم يكن واجب الوجود. كما أنه يمكن فهم هذه الصفة بالطريقة ذاتها التي نفهم بها صفة القدم، إذ كلا الصفتين لا مقياس في الخيال لها، وإن كان في العقل دليل على ثبوتها. فمن المستحيل أن يستطيع الخيال تصورهما وفهم حقيقتها وإن كان العقل يجزم في الوقت نفسه بثبوتها. وهكذا تعلم أن عدم قدرة العقل على تصور الشيء، ليس دليلاً على عدمه البتة كما هو واضح معلوم.
But that does not mean that the intellect is certain of its impossibility, for perhaps there is a matter which the intellect perceives its possibility or existence while at the same time it is incapable of imagining it and grasping its inner reality. 3 - (Al-Baqā'): Its meaning is the impossibility of non-existence attaching to His Essence, glorified and exalted be He. Its transmitted proof is the same verse which is the proof of al-qidam (eternity), namely His saying, exalted be He: "He is the First and the Last, the Outer and the Inner" [al-Hadid: 3]. And as for its rational proof, it is what we said in the proof of al-qidam. For just as it is inconceivable that there be an entity effecting existence in the Necessary Existent, so it is inconceivable that there be an entity effecting non-existence in Him, otherwise He would not be the Necessary Existent. Also, this attribute can be understood in the same way by which we understand the attribute of al-qidam, for both attributes have no measure in imagination, even though there is a rational proof of their affirmation. So it is impossible for imagination to conceive them and understand their reality, even though the intellect at the same time is certain of their affirmation. Thus you learn that the inability of the intellect to conceive a thing is not at all a proof of its non-existence, as is clear and known.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of al-baqā' (eternal duration) for Allah and provides proofs. The passage opens with a general principle: the intellect's inability to imagine something does not entail its impossibility. Then the author defines al-baqā' as the impossibility of non-existence attaching to Allah's essence. He gives two proofs: a transmitted proof (naqlī) from the Quranic verse 'He is the First and the Last...'—the same verse used for al-qidam—and a rational proof ('aqlī) parallel to that of al-qidam. The rational argument is that since Allah is the Necessary Existent (wājib al-wujūd), no external cause can bring Him into existence, and similarly no cause can annihilate Him; otherwise He would not be necessary. The author then explains that both al-qidam and al-baqā' are beyond imaginative grasp, yet reason affirms them. He concludes by reinforcing the principle: inability to conceive something is not evidence of its non-existence.

البقاء
القدم
واجب الوجود
دليل عقلي
دليل نقلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If the mind cannot imagine something, that thing cannot exist.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that inability to conceive something is not evidence of its non-existence. Many divine attributes are beyond imagination yet rationally proven.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the rational proof for al-baqā'?
A) Because Allah says 'He is the First and the Last'
B) Because no cause can annihilate the Necessary Existent
C) Because the intellect can imagine it
D) Because it is the same as al-qidam in every way

Key Takeaway
Al-baqā' is proven by Quran and reason, and the inability to imagine it does not count against its reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself doubting Allah's eternal existence because your mind cannot fully imagine it? How does this lesson call you to trust your intellect's certainty over your imagination's limitations? Will you actively remind yourself of this distinction when doubts arise?
?
If everything in creation will eventually perish except Allah, what does that mean for how you attach your heart to worldly things? Are there possessions, relationships, or ambitions you are holding onto as if they will last forever? What step can you take today to realign your attachment to the Eternal instead?
?
The proof for al-baqā' rests on the impossibility of non-existence for the Necessary Existent. How does your own contingent existence—your constant need for preservation—make you realize your utter dependence on al-Bāqī (the Everlasting)? In what specific area of your life have you been acting as if you are self-sufficient? What will you change today to acknowledge your need for Him?

Al-Qiyām bi al-Dhāt: The Self-Subsistence of Allah
Defines al-qiyām bi al-dhāt and gives its proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of al-qiyām bi al-dhāt and its proof from both the Quran and reason.

Core Idea
Allah depends on nothing; everything depends on Him.

The attribute of self-subsistence (al-qiyām bi al-dhāt) is foundational for understanding Allah's absolute independence. In this lesson, you will read al-Buti's concise definition and the evidence he presents, both from the Quran and from rational necessity. This prepares you to grasp why Allah cannot be compared to created beings.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation, focusing on the precise wording of 'not in need of a creator or substratum'.
Notice the use of 'qiyām bi al-dhāt' itself.
2
Understand the Quranic proof
The author cites the verse 'Allah is al-Ṣamad' and explains it as 'the One who does not need anything and everything needs Him'. Reflect on how this perfectly matches the definition.
3
Reflect on the rational proof
The rational proof follows from Allah being the Necessary Existent, eternal and unaffected. Ask yourself why this necessitates self-subsistence.
This argument is based on the nature of wujūb al-wujūd.
4
Connect to previous lessons
Recall that attributes like qiyām bi al-dhāt are essential to tawḥīd. This lesson solidifies the foundation for understanding divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤ - ( القيام بالذات ( أي إنه تعالى غير مفتقر إلى موجـد يـوجـده ولا إلى محل يقوم به . فقد كان الله تعالى قبل وجود أي شيء وقبل وجود الزمان ( أي الأفلاك التي تحد سير الوقت ) والمكان . والدليل على ثبوت هذه الصفة الله تعالى بالإضافة إلى دليل العقل الواضح قوله تعالى : ﴿ اللهُ الصَّمَدُ ﴾ أي الذي لا يحتاج إلى شيء ويحتاج إليه كل شيء . واعلم أنه لا مجال لتوقف العقل في إثبات هذه الصفة الله تعالى ، بعد معرفة أنه واجب الوجود وأنه قديم لا يتأثر بشيء ويتأثر به كل شيء .. فإن قلت : كيف أفهم أنه لا مكان لله ، والذي أعلمه أنه ما من موجود ، إلا وهو متحيز في مكان ما ؟ فالجواب أن علمك هذا إنما استقيته من استقراء حالات الأجسام والحوادث . والصفات المتلبسة بالأشياء الممكنة والحادثة لا يجب تلبسها بالواجب أيضاً . وإن رحت تقيس فذلك قياس لا برهان عليه ، إذ لا علة جامعة بين الأصل والفرع . بل العقل يوجب اختلاف واجب الوجود عن الممكنات في كل ذلك . ولا يضيرك بعد معرفة هذا أنك لا تستطيع أن تتخيل في ذهنك عدم تحيزه سبحانه وتعالى في مكان ، لأنك قد علمت أن الخيال ليس أكثر من مرآة تثبت فيها صور المرئيات التي مرت على حواسك . وهذا مما لم يمر على شيء من حواسك بعد ، فكيف تتخيله وتتصوره ؟ إنه لو ثبت الله مكان يتحدد فيه ، وأمكنك أن تتصوره في مكانه ذلك لكان عقلك أكبر إحاطة بالأشياء من إحاطة خالقها بها ، وذلك يدل على عدم ألوهيته . فكان طبيعياً من العقل إذا أن يستيقن ولا يتصور بل يحتار ويجهل . وليس شيئاً كثيراً في حقك أن تبلغ الحيرة بك في تصور الذات الإلهية مبلغ حيرتك في عقلك وروحك والطاقة التي جعلها الله تعالى سراً يقوم عليه وجود أكثر ما تراه حولك من الموجودات ، فأين هو مكان العقل أو الروح في جسمك وأين هو مستقر الحياة من الأشياء الحية وما هي حقيقتها ؟ لا تعلم ولا أحد يعلم الجواب، على الرغم من تيقن الجميع بوجود العقل والروح والحياة . إن الحيرة أمام هذه الأمور ضرورة ناتجة عن كون العقل محدوداً بالحدود التي أرادها له الخالق جل جلاله ، وكيف لا يحار المخلوق لدى محاولة تحليل خالقه وتصوره ؟!.. من أجل هذا كانت الحيرة - بعد الإيمان به وبصفاته سبـحـانـه وتعالى - أعلى مراتب الإيمان ، فحسبك أن تتيقن بوجوده ثم تحار في فهمه وتصوره . وتلك هي حقيقة ( الإيمان بالغيب ( الذي أمر الله به عباده . إذ هو أن يؤمنوا بما غاب عن محسوساتهم وعن عقولهم من حيث التحديد والتكييف لهذا.
4 - (Al-Qiyām bi al-Dhāt), meaning that He, exalted be He, is not in need of any being that brings Him into existence nor of any substratum in which He subsists. For Allah, exalted be He, existed before the existence of anything and before the existence of time (i.e., the spheres that define the course of time) and space. The proof of the affirmation of this attribute, in addition to the clear rational proof, is His saying, exalted be He: "Allah is al-Ṣamad" [al-Ikhlas: 2], i.e., the One who does not need anything and everything needs Him. Know that there is no room for hesitation of the intellect in affirming this attribute of Allah, exalted be He, after knowing that He is the Necessary Existent and that He is eternal, unaffected by anything and affecting everything. If you say: How can I understand that there is no place for Allah, while I know that there is no existent except that it occupies a place? The answer is that this knowledge of yours is derived only from surveying the states of bodies and contingent things. The attributes that clothe possible and contingent things do not necessarily clothe the Necessary Existent as well. And if you attempt analogy, it is an analogy without proof, for there is no common cause linking the original case and the branch. Rather, the intellect necessitates the difference of the Necessary Existent from all possibles in all that. And it does not harm you, after knowing this, that you cannot imagine in your mind His lack of occupying a place, glorified and exalted be He, because you have known that imagination is nothing but a mirror in which images of visible things that have passed through your senses are fixed. And this is something that has not passed through any of your senses, so how could you imagine it and conceive it? If it were established that Allah occupies a specific place, and you could conceive Him in that place, then your intellect would encompass things more than their Creator encompasses them, and that indicates the negation of His divinity. So it was natural for the intellect then to be certain but not to conceive; rather, it is perplexed and ignorant. And it is not too much for you that your perplexity in conceiving the Divine Essence reaches the level of your perplexity about your own intellect and soul and the energy that Allah, exalted be He, made a secret upon which the existence of most of the existents you see around you is based. For where is the place of the intellect or the soul in your body? Where is the seat of life in living things? And what is its reality? You do not know, and no one knows the answer, despite everyone's certainty of the existence of intellect, soul, and life. Indeed, perplexity before these matters is a necessity resulting from the intellect being limited by the limits that the Creator, majestic is His majesty, willed for it. And how could the created not be perplexed when attempting to analyze and conceive its Creator? For this reason, perplexity – after faith in Him and His attributes, glorified and exalted be He – is the highest rank of faith. It suffices you that you are certain of His existence, and then be perplexed in understanding and conceiving Him. That is the reality of (faith in the unseen) which Allah commanded His servants. That is, that they believe in what is hidden from their senses and from their intellects in terms of limiting and qualifying this.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute al-qiyām bi al-dhāt (self-subsistence) and addresses an objection about God's relation to place. The author defines it as Allah's independence from any creator or substratum; He existed before time and space. The transmitted proof is the verse 'Allah is al-Ṣamad' (the Self-Sufficient), and the rational proof follows from His being the Necessary Existent, independent and unaffected. An objection is raised: how can we understand that God has no place when every existent we know occupies place? The answer distinguishes between contingent things and the Necessary Existent; attributes of possibles do not necessarily apply to God. Analogy is invalid because there is no common cause. The author then explains that imagination is limited to sensory images, and since God is not sensed, He cannot be imagined. If we could imagine Him, our intellect would be greater than His, which is absurd. So the intellect must be certain but not imagine; it is natural to be perplexed (hayrah). This perplexity is compared to our perplexity about the nature of our own intellect, soul, and life. Such perplexity, after faith, is the highest rank of faith. This is the essence of faith in the unseen (al-ghayb): belief in what is beyond senses and intellectual delimitation.

Key Terms
القيام بالذات
الصمد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does al-qiyām bi al-dhāt mean according to the passage?
A) Allah is self-sufficient and does not need anything
B) Allah is not in need of a creator or a substratum
C) Allah is the only one who exists
D) Allah exists without beginning

Key Takeaway
Al-qiyām bi al-dhāt means Allah is independent of all things, proven by the Quran and the necessity of existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly rely on Allah as the only one who is self-sufficient, or do you secretly depend on created things to provide what only Allah can? What would it take for you to shift that reliance?
?
If Allah was in need of anything, He would not be Allah. Yet you often act as if you are independent from Him. How does this truth about Allah's self-subsistence expose the falsehood of your own sense of self-sufficiency?
?
The intellect has no room for hesitation in affirming this attribute. But do you live as if you believe it, or do your worries and anxieties show that you doubt His complete independence and ability to provide for you?
