الإرادة التنجيزية
تعلق الإرادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the will is multiple or changes.
Correction: The will is one and eternal; the difference is only in our consideration of whether it is attached to a specific object or not.

Checkpoint
What is the difference between the sanctioning will and the executive will?
A) The sanctioning will is temporal, the executive is eternal.
B) The sanctioning will is a capacity, the executive is actual attachment.
C) The sanctioning will is for good, the executive for evil.
D) They are two separate attributes.

Key Takeaway
The divine will is one eternal attribute; the distinction between sanctioning and executive is only a conceptual consideration of capacity versus actual attachment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at the course of your life, do you ever find yourself thinking that God's will has changed or that He might have wanted something else for you and then changed His mind? How does this lesson's truth that God's will is one eternal attribute, with no change or multiplicity, confront that subtle doubt? What specific step can you take today to anchor your heart in this reality when uncertainty strikes?
?
Have you ever treated the executive will of God (His actual decrees in your life) as separate from His sanctioning will (His eternal capacity), as if He might be willing something for you out of compulsion or reaction rather than from an eternal, unchanging purpose? How can you begin to see every event in your life as a direct manifestation of that single, eternal will, even when you do not understand it?
?
The lesson teaches that the distinction between sanctioning and executive will is only a conceptual consideration. How often do you unwittingly 'split' God's will in your mind, attributing different intentions to Him at different times, rather than resting in the unity of His eternal will? What practical habit can you adopt—such as a specific dhikr or a reflection at the start of each day—to remind yourself that God's will is one and unchanging, and that your trials and blessings alike flow from that same eternal source?

Why Is God’s Executive Will Eternal?
Answering an objection about the eternality of executive will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the executive attachment of God's will must be eternal and how the term 'tanjīz' applies to will versus power.

Core Idea
The executive will is eternal because it is based on God's eternal knowledge.

This passage tackles a common confusion: if God's will is called 'executive' (tanzīzī), doesn't that imply it is temporal? The author explains that 'executive' here refers to specific attachment, not temporal execution, and that the attachment must be eternal to align with God's eternal knowledge. Let's read the passage and see how the objection is resolved.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Begin by reading the objection: How can the executive attachment of God's will be eternal when we call it 'executive'?
The term 'tanjīzī' might mislead one to think it refers to temporal action.
2
Understand the answer
The answer states that the attachment must be eternal; otherwise, God would not have eternal knowledge of future acts, which is impossible.
This argument relies on the necessary connection between will and knowledge.
3
Clarify the term 'tanjīz'
The author distinguishes 'tanjīz' for will (specific attachment) from 'tanjīz' for power (actual creation). For will, it is merely a specific orientation, not temporal execution.
This removes the confusion that 'tanjīz' implies temporality.
4
Reflect on the human analogy
Consider the human example: a person may will an action long before executing it, yet that will is called executive because it is a real, specific intention.
This illustrates that executive will can be eternal in God's case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولعلك تسأل: فكيف يكون تعلق الإرادة الإلهية بالممكنات قديماً أيضاً، كالإرادة الصلوحية العامة، مع أننا نسميها بالتنجيزية؟ والجواب أن تعلق الإرادة الإلهية بإيجاد شيء أو إعدامه، قديم ولا يمكن أن يكون حادثاً. إذ لو كان كذلك، لكان من مستلزماته أن لا يكون الله عالماً ببعض ما يريد خلقه وفعله في المستقبل. وهو محال لما مرّ بيانه. فثبت عكسه إذاً: وهو أن الله يعلم في الأزل كل ما سيفعله وسيخلقه في الحين والوقت الملائمين، وهذا يعني بالبداهة أن إرادة الله التنجيزية مصاحبة لعلمه القديم هذا. بقي أن تعلم بأن الشبهة إنما تحوم حول فكرك، من كلمة إذا تتخيل أن معناها الخلق والظهور وهو شيء حادث قطعاً، غير أن هذا صحيح بالنسبة للقدرة التي سنتحدث عنها. أما الإرادة فالتنجيز بالنسبة لها هو محض تعلقها بممكن من الممكنات، سواء ظهر هذا الممكن إلى طور الوجود أم لم يظهر بعد. وقد تتعلق إرادة الإنسان بعمل من الأعمال، ثم يطويه عن التنفيذ إلى بعد سنوات كثيرة فتسمى إرادته هذه تنجيزية، أي ليست مجرد قابلية محضة، بل هي توجه فعلي إلى مراد معين.
Perhaps you will ask: How can the attachment of the divine will to possibles also be eternal, like the general sanctioning will, when we call it executive? The answer: The attachment of the divine will to bringing something into existence or annihilating it is eternal and cannot be originated. For if it were originated, it would entail that God is not knowledgeable about some of what He intends to create and do in the future. That is impossible, as has been explained. Thus its opposite is established: that God knows in pre-eternity everything He will do and create at the appropriate time and moment, and this necessarily means that God's executive will accompanies His eternal knowledge. It remains for you to know that the doubt only circles around your mind because of the word [tanzīz], imagining that it means creation and manifestation, which is definitely originated. However, this is correct with respect to power, which we will discuss. As for the will, tanzīz with respect to it is merely its attachment to a possible among possibles, whether or not that possible has emerged into the realm of existence. And the will of a human may attach to an action, then he postpones its execution for many years, yet his will is called executive, i.e., not mere potentiality, but an actual orientation towards a specific object of will.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer. The objector asks: How can the executive attachment (ta'alluq tanjīzī) be eternal when we call it 'executive' implying temporal action? The answer explains that the attachment is eternal because if it were temporal, God would not have eternal knowledge of future acts, which is impossible. Therefore, the executive attachment is eternal, accompanying God's eternal knowledge. The author further clarifies that the term 'tanjīz' does not mean actual creation (that applies to power), but rather the specific attachment of the will to a particular possible, regardless of when it occurs. This is illustrated by a human willing an action long before executing it, yet that will is still called executive because it is a real orientation, not mere potentiality.

Key Terms
تعلق تنجيزي
علم قديم
إرادة إلهية
قدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term 'executive' (tanjīzī) implies that the will itself is temporal and occurs at the moment of creation.
Correction: For God's will, 'tanjīz' means specific attachment to a possible, not temporal execution. The attachment is eternal, accompanying God's eternal knowledge.

Checkpoint
Why must the executive attachment of God's will be eternal?
A) Because God's will is changeless.
B) Because otherwise God would lack eternal knowledge of future acts.
C) Because humans also have executive will that is eternal.
D) Because the will is one with God's essence.

Key Takeaway
The executive will is eternal because it is based on God's eternal knowledge, and 'tanjīz' denotes specific attachment, not temporal action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage teaches that God's will is eternally attached to every action you take, even those you delay for years. What does this mean about your excuses for procrastinating on good deeds? Will you today commit to one action you have postponed, trusting that God's eternal will has already specified it?
?
If God's knowledge encompasses every future event, including your failures and sins, does that calm your fear of the unknown or expose your lack of reliance on Him? How will you actively trust His timing in a situation you are currently anxious about?
?
The author distinguishes between will and execution: God's will is not the same as immediate creation. How does that distinction challenge your impatience when prayers seem unanswered? In what specific area of your life do you need to surrender your timeline to God's eternal plan?

Rational Proof for the Divine Will
Sanusi presents a rational proof for the will using necessary implication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof for the attribute of will in God, based on the necessity of avoiding compulsion.

Core Idea
Without will, God would be compelled, contradicting His necessary existence.

This passage presents a concise rational argument for the divine will. It uses a logical necessity argument: if will were not eternal in God, then the opposite—compulsion—would be necessary. But compulsion requires a compeller, which is impossible for the Necessary Existence. Let's examine the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the rational proof passage
Read the first part of the source passage carefully. It contains a single logical argument from necessity.
Notice the phrase 'اللزوم البيّن' which indicates this is a clear necessary inference.
2
Understand the conditional statement
The argument begins with a conditional: if will (the attribute) were not existent and eternal in God, then its opposite (compulsion) would be necessary.
Compulsion (الإكراه) means being forced to act without choice.
3
Identify the consequence of compulsion
Compulsion implies the existence of a compeller (مكرِه). This is a logical implication.
If something is compelled, there must be something that compels it.
4
Grasp the final contradiction
A compeller would be external to God, which contradicts God's status as Necessary Existence and the meaning of divinity (الألوهية). Therefore, the original assumption that will is not eternal is false.
The conclusion is that will must be an eternal attribute of God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودليل هذه الصفة من العقل اللزوم البيّن أيضاً، إذ لو لم تكن موجودة وأزلية فيه سبحانه وتعالى للزم عليه نقيضها وهو الإكراه، وهو يستلزم مكرهاً، وذلك ينافي واجب الوجود ومعنى الألوهية.
ودليلها من النقل، آيات كثيرة من مثل قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَمَنْ يُرِدِ فِتْنَتَهُ فَلَنْ تَمْلِكَ لَهُ مِنَ اللهِ شَيْئاً ﴾ [المائدة: ٤١] وقوله: ﴿ وَإِذَا أَرَادَ اللهُ بِقَوْمٍ سُوءاً فَلَا مَرَدَّ لَهُ وَمَا لَهُمْ مِنْ دُونِهِ مِنْ وَالٍ ﴾ [الرعد: ١١].
And the proof of this attribute from reason is the evident necessity as well: for if it [the will] were not existent and eternal in Him, Exalted is He, then its opposite, which is compulsion, would be necessary for Him, and that necessitates a compeller, and that contradicts the Necessary Existence and the meaning of divinity.
And its proof from transmitted evidence is many verses, such as His statement, Exalted: 'And whoever desires his fitnah – you will never possess for him from Allah anything' [5:41], and His statement: 'And when Allah intends for a people evil, there is no repelling it, and they have besides Him no protector' [13:11].
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage provides two proofs for the divine attribute of will: rational and scriptural. The rational proof is by way of necessity (luzūm): if will were not eternal in God, then the opposite – compulsion (ikrāh) – would be necessary, meaning God would be compelled, which requires a compeller, contradicting His necessary existence and divinity. The scriptural proof cites two Quranic verses that explicitly affirm God's will: one from Surah al-Ma'ida (5:41) showing God's will regarding fitnah, and another from Surah al-Ra'd (13:11) showing that when God wills punishment, it cannot be repelled. These verses demonstrate that God has a will that is effective.

Key Terms
دليل العقل
الإكراه
واجب الوجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God does not have will, He acts by natural necessity, which is acceptable.
Correction: Without will, God would be compelled by an external force, not natural necessity. This requires a compeller, which is impossible for the Necessary Existence.

Checkpoint
What does the rational proof for the will conclude?
A) Without will, God would be ignorant.
B) Without will, God would be compelled, contradicting necessary existence.
C) Without will, God would be weak.
D) Without will, God would not create.

Key Takeaway
The rational proof shows that God must have will because otherwise He would be compelled, which is incompatible with His necessary existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that God's will is eternal and not subject to compulsion, would you still make excuses for your sins by blaming circumstances beyond your control? How can you align your life with this truth today?
?
Do you live as though God's will is active in every detail of your life, or do you sometimes act as if things happen by mere chance? What would change if you fully internalized that nothing escapes His will?
?
When you face a difficult decision, do you seek God's will with the same urgency as if you were being forced? Or do you rely on your own plans? Commit to one concrete step this week to prioritize His will over your own.

Scriptural Proof for the Divine Will
Sanusi cites two Quranic verses as scriptural proof for the will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran provides scriptural evidence for the divine will through verses that affirm God's will and its effectiveness.

Core Idea
The Quran explicitly affirms that God has an effective will over all things.

After the rational proof, the author provides scriptural evidence from the Quran. Two verses are cited that clearly show God's will in action: one concerning fitnah and another concerning punishment. These verses demonstrate that God's will is real and cannot be thwarted.

Guided Path
1
Read the scriptural proof passage
Read the second part of the source passage. It introduces the scriptural proof and cites two Quranic verses.
Notice that the author says there are many verses, then gives two examples.
2
Examine the first verse
Look at the verse from Surah al-Ma'ida (5:41): 'And whoever intends his fitnah, you will never be able to do anything for him against Allah.' This shows that God's will regarding someone's trial is decisive.
The verse implies that no one can alter what God wills for a person's trial.
3
Examine the second verse
Look at the verse from Surah al-Ra'd (13:11): 'And when Allah intends evil for a people, there is no repelling it.' This shows that God's will to punish is irresistible.
The verse emphasizes that God's will cannot be prevented or reversed.
4
Connect the verses to the attribute of will
Both verses explicitly use the verb 'يريد' (He wills) in relation to God, confirming that God has a will that is effective and central to His actions.
These verses serve as textual evidence for the attribute of will.

Divine Will and Command Are Distinct
Clarifies that will and command are distinct and separable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine will and command are distinct attributes with no necessary connection, as affirmed by Ahl al-Sunnah.

Core Idea
God's will and command are not always the same—they can be separate.

This lesson tackles a subtle but important distinction in Islamic theology: the difference between what God wills and what He commands. While some may assume they always coincide, the People of the Sunnah teach that they can be separate. Understanding this distinction is key to grasping other doctrinal truths, as the author promises to elaborate later.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text and its translation to get the author's point directly.
Notice the key terms al-irāda and al-amr.
2
Understand the core claim
The passage states that will and command are different and separable. Reflect on why this matters.
The phrase 'as is imagined' suggests a common misconception.
3
Connect to Ahl al-Sunnah
Note that this position is attributed to Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jamā'ah. This anchors the teaching in mainstream Sunni theology.
4
Look ahead
The author promises to elaborate later. Consider what implications this distinction might have for understanding divine actions.
E.g., how does this relate to the story of Iblis? He was commanded to prostrate but perhaps it was not willed? We'll see.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لا بد أن تعلم أن الإرادة والأمر متغايران، ومنفكان. فلا لزوم بينهما كما يتصور، على ما حققه أهل السنة والجماعة. وموعدنا معك في شرح هذا التغاير وبيانه، عند الحديث عما يترتب على معرفة هذه الصفات من الحقائق الاعتقادية.
Then you must know that will and command are different and separable. There is no necessary connection between them as is imagined, according to what the People of the Sunnah and Community have verified. And our appointment with you to explain this difference and clarify it is when we discuss what follows from knowing these attributes in terms of doctrinal truths.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage makes a brief but important theological point: the divine will (al-irāda) and the divine command (al-amr) are two distinct things, not necessarily linked. For example, God may command something without willing it (like testing), or will something without commanding it (like some events). This position is affirmed by Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jamā'ah. The author promises to elaborate later when discussing theological implications.

Key Terms
الإرادة
الأمر
أهل السنة والجماعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God's will and command are always necessarily connected.
Correction: They are actually distinct and separable, as Ahl al-Sunnah affirm.

Checkpoint

A) They are identical.
B) They are inseparable.
C) They are different and separable.

Key Takeaway
Divine will and command are distinct attributes with no necessary connection—a key Sunni theological principle.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

How does this reality affect your view of divine justice and your own responsibility to call others? Does it deepen your gratitude for your own faith?

The Divine Attribute of Power: Definition and Two Attachments
Defines power and divides it into sanctioning and executive attachments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of divine power and its two attachments: the eternal sanctioning capacity and the temporal executive act.

Core Idea
Divine power is one eternal attribute with two aspects: eternal capacity and temporal execution.

Having understood divine will, we now turn to another essential attribute: power. Like will, power has a dual consideration. But while the will's executive attachment is eternal, power's executive attachment is temporal. This passage defines power and clarifies this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice how the author uses conditional language: 'If you observe...' to distinguish the two attachments.
2
Identify the two attachments
Find where the passage describes the sanctioning attachment (ta'alluq ṣulūḥī) and the executive attachment (ta'alluq tanjīzī). Note their different temporal statuses.
The sanctioning attachment is eternal; the executive attachment is originated.
3
Reflect on the unity of power
Understand why the author emphasises that power itself is one and eternal despite the two attachments. Ask: How does this relate to the attribute of will?
The passage concludes that both attachments go back to one power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
3 - (القدرة) وهي صفة أزلية قائمة بذاته تعالى يتأتى بها إيجاد كل ممكن وإعدامه وتكييفه. ثم إنك إن لاحظت هذه الصفة من حيث هي معنى أزلي قائم بذاته تعالى، صالح لأن يوجد به الممكنات أو يعدمها أو يكيفها، بقطع النظر عن التنفيذ، فتلك القدرة التي تتعلق بالأشياء تعلقاً صلوحياً فقط. وإن لاحظت تنفيذ الإيجاد والإعدام أو التكييف الفعلي، فتلك القدرة الإلهية في تعلقها التنجيزي.
وبذلك تعلم أن القدرة واحدة أيضاً. فإن نظرت إلى تعلقها الصلوحي فهو تعلق أزلي قديم، وإن نظرت إلى تعلقها التنجيزي فهو تعلق حادث. أي إن كلا التعلقين عائدان إلى قدرة واحدة، وإنما الحادث هو التعلق التنجيزي بالأشياء، أما القدرة ذاتها فهي قديمة على كل حال.
3 – Power: It is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, Exalted, by which the bringing into existence, annihilating, and qualifying of every possible is effected. Then if you observe this attribute from the aspect that it is an eternal meaning subsisting in His essence, Exalted, suitable for bringing possibles into existence, annihilating them, or qualifying them, regardless of execution, that is the power that relates to things only as a sanctioning attachment. And if you observe the execution of bringing into existence, annihilating, or actual qualifying, that is the divine power in its executive attachment. And thereby you know that power is also one. For if you consider its sanctioning attachment, it is an eternal, pre-eternal attachment; and if you consider its executive attachment, it is an originated attachment. That is, both attachments go back to one power, and the only originated thing is the executive attachment to things, while power itself is eternal in any case.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the divine attribute of power (al-qudra). It is eternal and subsists in God's essence, enabling Him to create, annihilate, or qualify any possible thing. Like the will, power also has two considerations: the sanctioning attachment (ta'alluq ṣulūḥī) – the mere capacity to act, which is eternal; and the executive attachment (ta'alluq tanjīzī) – the actual performance, which is temporal. The author emphasizes that power itself is one and eternal; only the executive attachment to specific things comes into being when the act occurs. This parallels the earlier discussion on will, but with a key difference: the executive attachment of power is temporally originated, whereas that of will is eternal.

Key Terms
القدرة
القدرة الصلوحية
القدرة التنجيزية
تعلق صلوحي
تعلق تنجيزي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that because there are two attachments, there are two powers or that power itself changes.
Correction: Power is a single eternal attribute. The attachments are different ways of considering the same power; the executive attachment is temporal but does not affect the eternity of power itself.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of the executive attachment (al-ta'alluq al-tanjīzī) of divine power?
A) It is eternal like the sanctioning attachment.
B) It is originated (ḥādith).
C) It is both eternal and originated.
D) It is neither eternal nor originated.

Key Takeaway
Divine power is one eternal attribute; its capacity is eternal, but its actual execution in time is originated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe that God's power is eternal and complete, even before He acts. But when you pray for something urgent and don't see immediate change, do you truly trust that His power is already fully capable, or do you doubt His ability until you see the result? How will you remind yourself today that His power is not dependent on execution?
?
Consider a sin you struggle with. Do you believe that God's power to help you overcome it is already present, or do you feel that He has not yet 'activated' that power? What would change in your struggle if you internalized that His power to transform you is eternally ready, and only the execution awaits His will?
?
The lesson teaches that God's power has two aspects: the eternal capacity and the temporal act. Which of these two aspects do you neglect when making du'a? Do you focus more on the moment of the answer or on the eternal reality of His ability? How can you shift your heart to rely on His eternal power today?

Definition of the Divine Attribute of Hearing
Defines the divine hearing as an eternal attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of the divine attribute of hearing (al-samʿ) as an eternal, perfect perception that does not involve imagination or physical means.

Core Idea
God's hearing is eternal and complete, not dependent on ears or air.

This lesson introduces the divine attribute of hearing as understood in the Ashʿarī tradition. The passage defines hearing as an eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence, relating to all audibles or existents. It emphasizes that God's hearing is perfect and unlike human hearing, which relies on sense organs and physical processes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the key terms.
2
Understand the definition
The passage defines hearing as an eternal attribute. Identify its relation (to audibles or existents) and the nature of perception (perfect, not via imagination or senses).
3
Reflect on the distinction
Contrast God's hearing with human hearing. Why is it important to affirm that God's hearing is not like ours?
This safeguards transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
4 - (السمع) وهو صفة أزلية قائمة بذاته تعالى تتعلق بالمسموعات، أو بالموجودات، فتدرك إدراكاً تاماً لا على طريق التخيل والتوهم ولا على طريق تأثير حاسة ووصول هواء.
4 – Hearing: It is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, Exalted, relating to audibles, or to existents, and it perceives a complete perception not by way of imagination and fancy nor by way of the effect of a sense organ or the arrival of air.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of hearing (al-sam'). It is eternal, subsisting in God. It relates to what is heard (al-masmū'āt) or perhaps to all existents (al-mawjūdāt). The perception is perfect and complete, unlike human hearing which requires airwaves and sense organs. God's hearing is not through imagination or physical means, affirming His transcendence.

Definition of Divine Power and Its Two Relations
Buti defines al-Qudra and distinguishes its two forms of relation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of divine power as an eternal attribute and the distinction between its potential and actual relations.

Core Idea
God’s power is one, but relates to creation in two modes: potential (eternal) and actual (temporal).

Buti begins by defining al-Qudra, the divine attribute of power, as an eternal quality subsisting in God’s essence. He then clarifies that this single power relates to possible things in two distinct ways: as a mere capacity (potential relation) and as actual execution (actual relation). Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping how God's eternal attribute can produce temporal acts without change in His essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to grasp the author's exact wording. Note the key terms: al-qudra, ta‘alluq ṣulūḥī, ta‘alluq tanjīzī.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the two relations
Locate where Buti distinguishes the two ways of considering power: as a mere suitability (potential) and as actual execution (actual). Notice how he defines each with the same power remaining one.
3
Reflect on the temporal vs eternal aspect
Consider why the potential relation is described as eternal (azalī) while the actual relation is temporal (ḥādith). This preserves God’s attribute as unchanging while allowing for temporal acts.
Connect to the misconception that power changes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
3 - ( القدرة ) وهي صفة أزلية قائمة بذاته تعالى يتأتى بها إيجاد كل ممكن وإعدامه وتكييفه . ثم إنك إن لاحظت هذه الصفة من حيث هي معنى أزلي قائم بذاته تعالى ، صالح لأن يوجد به الممكنات أو يعدمها أو يكيفها ، بقطع النظر عن التنفيذ ، فتلك القدرة التي تتعلق بالأشياء تعلقاً صلوحيـاً فقط . وإن لاحظت تنفيذ الإيجاد والإعدام أو التكييف الفعلي ، فتلك القدرة الإلهية في تعلقها التنجيزي . هي هي وبذلك تعلم أن القدرة واحدة أيضاً. فإن نظرت إلى تعلقها الصلوحي فهو تعلق أزلي قديم وإن نظرت إلى تعلقها التنجيزي فهو تعلق حادث . أي إن كلا التعلقين عائدان إلى قدرة واحدة ، وإنما الحادث هو التعلق التنجيزي بالأشياء أما القدرة ذاتها فهي قديمة على كل حال
3 - (Power) It is an eternal attribute subsisting in His Essence, by which the creation, annihilation, and conditioning of every possible thing is effected. Then if you consider this attribute in that it is an eternal meaning subsisting in His Essence, suitable for creating, annihilating, or conditioning possibles, regardless of execution, then that is the power that relates to things only with a potential relation (taʿalluq ṣulūḥī). And if you consider the execution of creation, annihilation, or actual conditioning, then that is the divine power in its actual relation (taʿalluq tanjīzī). It is it. And by that you know that power is also one. For if you look at its potential relation, it is an eternal, ancient relation; and if you look at its actual relation, it is a temporal relation. That is, both relations go back to one power, and the temporal is only the actual relation to things, while power itself is eternal in any case.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the divine attribute of power (al-qudra). Buti states that power is an eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence, by which He creates, annihilates, and conditions every possible thing. He then distinguishes two ways of considering this attribute: First, considering power as a mere capacity or suitability (ṣalāḥiyya) without regard to actual execution—this is called the potential relation (al-taʿalluq al-ṣulūḥī). Second, considering power as actually creating, annihilating, or conditioning—this is called the actual relation (al-taʿalluq al-tanjīzī). Buti emphasizes that power itself is one, but its relations differ: the potential relation is eternal, while the actual relation is temporal (ḥādith). This preserves God's attribute as eternal while allowing for temporal acts. The phrase "هي هي" may be a scribal emphasis meaning "it is it"—i.e., it is still the same power in both cases.

Key Terms
القدرة (al-qudra)
تعلق صلوحي (taʿalluq ṣulūḥī)
تعلق تنجيزي (taʿalluq tanjīzī)
أزلي (azalī)
حادث (ḥādith)
ممكن (mumkin)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that the attribute of power becomes temporal when He acts, or that the potential relation implies deficiency.
Correction: Buti explains that power is one eternal attribute; only its actual relation to things is temporal. The potential relation is eternal and does not imply any deficiency.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, how many powers does God have?
A) Two: one eternal and one temporal.
B) One power with two different relations.
C) Separate powers for each possible thing.
D) Only a potential power.

Key Takeaway
God’s power is a single eternal attribute that relates to possible things in two ways: an eternal potential relation and a temporal actual relation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God’s power is eternally sufficient (potential relation) before He ever acts, why do you secretly doubt He can change your situation? Identify one area where you have limited God’s power because you measured it by your timeline. Today, write down that area and repent from demanding execution on your terms; trust that His power is already enough.
?
The actual relation of God’s power occurs in time, but His power itself is never new. How does your impatience with God’s delay expose a failure to believe in the perfection of His eternal capacity? Commit to waiting with the confidence that His power was already ready for your need before you were born.
?
Your dua often begs God to ‘activate’ His power, as if it were dormant. How does this lesson reveal the arrogance of that mindset? Repent from treating God’s power as reactive. Instead, thank Him that His power has always been perfectly suited for your situation, even before you asked.

Divine Hearing and Sight: Definitions, Proof, and Dispute
Buti defines hearing and sight, cites their proof from revelation, and presents a scholarly dispute on their scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definitions of divine hearing and sight according to Buti, their scriptural proof, and the scholarly disagreement on their scope.

Core Idea
God's hearing and sight are eternal, perfect perceptions, not physical senses.

This lesson examines two more divine attributes: hearing and sight. Buti defines them as eternal attributes subsisting in God's essence, perceiving perfectly without physical means. He grounds them firmly in revelation and presents a key scholarly dispute on whether they encompass all existents or only audibles/visibles.

Guided Path
1
Read the definitions of hearing and sight
Read the Arabic definitions for attributes 4 and 5. Notice how each is described as eternal, subsisting in God's essence, and relating to all things (or to their specific objects) with perfect perception.
The definitions avoid any suggestion of physical organs or processes.
2
Note the emphasis on perfect perception without physicality
Buti stresses that divine perception is not by imagination, illusion, or through senses like air or rays. Understand that this distinguishes God's attributes from human senses.
3
Understand the proof from revelation
Buti states these attributes are derived from transmitted proof (naql) from Quran and Sunna. This also explains why taste, smell, and touch are not attributed—no revelation establishes them.
Contrast with attributes like hearing and sight that are explicitly mentioned.
4
Examine the scholarly dispute on scope
Read the two views: al-Bājūrī and al-Sanūsī say hearing and sight encompass all existents; al-Taftāzānī says they relate to audibles and visibles. Buti's conclusion is to affirm both attributes and their distinct functions without specifying the exact scope.
Reflect on why Buti does not firmly side with one view.

4 - (Hearing) It is an eternal attribute subsisting in His Essence, relating to audible things, or to existing things, so it perceives with complete perception, not by way of imagination or illusion, nor by way of the effect of a sense or the arrival of air. 5 - (Sight) It is also an eternal attribute subsisting in His Essence, relating to visible things or existing things, so it perceives with complete perception, not by way of imagination or illusion, nor by way of the affection of a sense or the arrival of a ray. And know that His description, may His majesty be exalted, with these two attributes is only derived from the transmitted proof (dalīl al-naql) established with certainty in both the Book and the Sunna, such that no rational person can deny or reinterpret. And adherence to the transmitted proof in this is what prevented us from attributing to Him, glorified and exalted, the attributes of taste, smell, and touch, since no proof from transmission has come to establish them via a sense or an instrument as is the case for humans and animals. Indeed, the scholars differed on the scope of each of these two attributes. Some of them, like al-Bājūrī and al-Sanūsī, said that they encompass all existing things, with different meanings in each. That is, His hearing relates to what is audible for us and to what is not audible from the rest of existing things, and similarly His sight. And some, like Sa‘d al-Dīn al-Taftāzānī (may God have mercy on him), said: The attribute of hearing relates to audible things, and the attribute of sight relates to visible things. What is appropriate to stop at in this regard is to believe in the affirmation of these two attributes for Him, glorified and exalted, according to what He described Himself with, then to believe that each of these two attributes has a function distinct from the other. Otherwise, there would be no meaning in ascribing each of them separately to Him other than repetition, and that is impossible in this context. As for the reality of each of these two attributes and their scope, and whether each has a special function related to some existing things as is the case for us, or are they (1) We relied in defining these two attributes on the commentary of ‘Abd al-Salām on Jawharat al-Tawḥīd, Itḥāf al-Murīd: 123, 107.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage defines two more divine attributes: hearing (al-sam‘) and sight (al-basar). Buti defines each as an eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence, relating to all things (or to their specific objects) with perfect perception, not through physical organs or processes like imagination, illusion, or the arrival of air/rays. He emphasizes that these attributes are proven solely by transmitted revelation (al-naql) from the Qur’an and Sunna, and are not derived from reason. Consequently, he explains that we do not attribute taste, smell, or touch to God because no revelation establishes them via sensory means as with creatures. Then Buti presents a scholarly dispute: al-Bājūrī and al-Sanūsī hold that hearing and sight encompass all existents, each in a different sense (i.e., God hears everything, even what we cannot hear, and sees everything). Al-Taftāzānī holds that hearing relates to audibles and sight to visibles (i.e., their objects are restricted to what is by nature audible/visible). Buti does not definitively side with one view; instead, he concludes that what is obligatory is to affirm both attributes, to believe each has a distinct function (otherwise separate mention would be redundant), while leaving the exact scope as known to God. The footnote indicates the definitions are taken from ‘Abd al-Salām’s commentary on Jawharat al-Tawḥīd.

Key Terms
السمع (al-sam‘)
البصر (al-basar)
النقل (al-naql)
قطعي (qaṭ‘ī)
باجوري (al-Bājūrī)
سنوسي (al-Sanūsī)
تفتنازاني (al-Taftāzānī)
إدراك (idrāk)
تخيل (takhayyul)
توهم (tawahhum)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Assuming God's hearing and sight are similar to human senses involving physical organs, or that the absence of a specific object (e.g., a non-audible thing) means God does not perceive it.
Correction: Buti emphasizes that divine hearing and sight are perfect perceptions not through physical means, and some scholars hold they encompass all existents, not just audibles/visibles.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, why are the attributes of taste, smell, and touch not attributed to God?
A) Reason proves they are impossible.
B) There is no transmitted proof establishing them.
C) They would imply deficiency.
D) They are incompatible with God's nature.

Key Takeaway
The attributes of hearing and sight are proven solely by revelation and are not physical; the exact scope is known to God, but each has a distinct function, avoiding redundancy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God sees and hears every action, thought, and intention of yours, as He describes Himself? If you did, how would your private moments change right now?

The passage says God's hearing and sight are not through senses or imagination. How does that challenge your mental image of God? Are you comfortable with a God whose perception is beyond your comprehension, or do you secretly wish He were more 'like us' so you could feel you understand Him?

How We Know Allah Has Hearing and Sight
Establishes the proof of hearing and sight through definitive texts and excludes other senses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the attributes of hearing and sight are known through definitive transmitted texts, not through sensory or imaginative means.

Core Idea
Allah's hearing and sight are known through revelation, not through senses or analogy with creation.

This lesson begins the discussion of two of Allah's attributes: hearing and sight. The author establishes that our knowledge of these attributes comes exclusively from definitive texts of the Qur'an and Sunnah. Unlike human senses, they are not understood through imagination or sensory experience. This principle also explains why we do not attribute other senses like taste or smell to Allah.

1
Read the opening passage
Read the Arabic passage that defines how Allah's hearing and sight are perceived. Note the negation of imagination and sensory influence.

And adherence to the transmitted proof in this is what prevented us from attributing to Him, glorified and exalted be He, the attribute of taste, smell, and touch, since no transmitted proof has come establishing them by way of a sense or an organ, as is the case with humans and animals. Indeed, the scholars differed regarding the extent of inclusiveness of each of these two attributes. Some of them, like al-Bajuri and al-Sanusi, said that they are inclusive of all existents, with the meaning differing in each. That is, His hearing pertains to what is audible for us and what is not audible from the rest of existents, and similarly His sight. And some, like Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The attribute of hearing pertains to sounds and the attribute of sight pertains to visible things. What we should stop at in this regard is faith in the establishment of these two attributes for Him, glorified and exalted be He, in accordance with what He has described Himself with, then faith that each of these two attributes has a function that distinguishes it from the other. Otherwise, there would be no meaning in attributing each of them separately to Him, exalted is He, other than repetition, and that is impossible in this context. As for the reality of each of these two attributes and their extent of inclusiveness, and whether each has a specific function related to some existents as is the case with us, or they are, (1) We relied in the definition of these two attributes on the commentary of 'Abd al-Salam on Jawharat al-Tawhid, 'Itthaf al-Murid: -123 - +9 and 107, in relation to Him, glorified and exalted be He, based on other and more comprehensive functions? — We entrust knowledge of that to Allah, glorified and exalted be He. And sufficient for us in such matters, for which the intellect has no access to affirmation or denial except reliance on certain transmitted reports and definitive texts, is that we stop at what these texts necessitate. And that is the way of the salaf, may Allah have mercy on them, in understanding the realities of Islamic creed.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is a combined explanation and recommendation regarding the divine attributes of hearing (sam') and sight (basar). It begins by stating that these attributes are known through definitive transmitted texts (naql qat'i) from the Qur'an and Sunnah, not through sensory or imaginative means. The author emphasizes that this reliance on transmitted proof is why we do not attribute to Allah things like taste, smell, or touch, since no such definitive text exists. Next, the author reports a scholarly difference: al-Bajuri and al-Sanusi hold that these attributes encompass all existents (with different meanings for each), while al-Taftazani holds that hearing is only for audible sounds and sight for visible objects. The author then advises the proper stance: to affirm the attributes as Allah describes Himself, and to believe that each has a distinct function, otherwise it would be redundant to mention them separately. Finally, the author addresses the reality and extent of these attributes, saying that whether they function specifically (like ours) or more broadly is a matter to entrust to Allah. The intellect cannot independently prove or deny in such matters; we must rely on definitive texts and stop at what they require. This is described as the method of the salaf (pious predecessors). The passage includes a footnote reference to a definition based on a commentary on Jawharat al-Tawhid.

Key Terms
السمع
البصر
النقل القطعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that Allah's hearing and sight are like human hearing and sight, known through sensory analogy.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that these attributes are known through definitive texts, not through imagination or sensory means. They are not understood by analogy with creation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do we not attribute the senses of taste, smell, and touch to Allah?
A) Because humans lack those senses.
B) Because no definitive transmitted proof establishes them.
C) Because they are not mentioned in the Qur'an at all.
D) Because they are not perfect attributes.

Key Takeaway
Allah's attributes of hearing and sight are affirmed through definitive revelation, not through sensory analogy, and other senses are not attributed due to lack of texts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you affirm that Allah hears and sees, do you ever catch yourself imagining a human-like ear or eye? What steps can you take today to replace that image with the conviction that His hearing and sight are known only through revelation?
?
Are you willing to accept that your knowledge of Allah's attributes is limited to what the Quran and Sunnah explicitly state? Is there any attribute you wish to affirm or deny for Allah that has no textual basis, and how does this lesson challenge that desire?
?
This passage says no transmitted proof exists for taste, smell, and touch – and we simply stop. Does your soul feel content with not knowing everything about Allah, or does it crave to go beyond revelation? What does this reveal about your trust in Allah's wisdom in revealing only what we need?

The Scope of Divine Hearing and Sight: Scholarly Disagreement and Proper Stance
Reports scholarly disagreement on the scope of hearing and sight and prescribes the proper attitudinal stance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly disagreement about the scope of Allah's hearing and sight, and the recommended approach of affirming them without delving into unnecessary detail.

Core Idea
Affirm Allah's hearing and sight as He describes, and entrust their full reality to Him.

This lesson continues from the previous one, now addressing the extent of inclusiveness of Allah's hearing and sight. Scholars have differed: some say they encompass all existents, others confine them to sounds and visible things. The author guides us to a middle path: to affirm each attribute has a distinct function, and to entrust the deeper reality to Allah, following the method of the salaf.

Guided Path
1
Read the disagreement
Read the passage where the author presents two scholarly views on the scope of hearing and sight.
2
Identify the two positions
Note the views of al-Bajuri and al-Sanusi (all-encompassing) and of al-Taftazani (specific to sounds/visible things).
3
Understand the recommended approach
The author advises faith in the attributes as Allah describes, belief in distinct functions, and entrusting the full reality to Allah.
4
Apply the salaf methodology
Recognize that this is the way of the salaf: stopping at the texts without over-interpretation.

The Eternal Attribute of Speech: Definition and Proof
Defines the attribute of speech and provides its scriptural proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of Allah's attribute of speech as an eternal attribute and the scriptural proofs for its existence.

Core Idea
Allah's speech is an eternal attribute, proven by Qur'an and hadith.

This lesson introduces the sixth divine attribute: speech (kalam). It defines kalam as an eternal attribute subsisting in Allah's essence, through which He commands, forbids, and informs. The author then provides definitive textual evidence from the Qur'an and authentic hadith to establish this attribute. Understanding this foundation is essential before considering how Allah's speech relates to the revealed scriptures.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition carefully
Notice the precise wording: 'صفة أزلية قائمة بذاته' (an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence). This implies that speech is not created but a necessary characteristic of Allah.
Also note that through this attribute, Allah commands, forbids, and informs.
2
Examine the three textual proofs
Identify each proof: Qur'an 4:164 (Allah spoke to Moses directly), Qur'an 9:6 (hearing the speech of Allah), and the hadith of the Night of Mi'raj (Prophet spoke to Allah and prayers were prescribed).
These are definitive texts (نصوص قطعية) that establish the attribute.
3
Reflect on the significance
Why is it important that speech is eternal? This distinguishes it from created beings and emphasizes that the Qur'an is the expression of an eternal attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٦ - ( الكلام ) وهو صفة أزلية قائمة بذاته تعالى ، هو بها آمر وناه ومخبر ، عبر عنها نظم ما أوحاه إلى رسله كالقرآن والتوراة والإنجيل • فأما دليل ثبوت هذه الصفة الله تعالى فالنصوص القطعية الثابتة في كل من الكتاب والسنة ، منها قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَكَلَّمَ الله موسى تكليماً ﴾ [ النساء : ١٦٤] وقوله جل جلاله ﴿ وإنْ أَحَدٌ مِنَ المُشركينَ اسْتَجَارَكَ فَأَجْرُهُ حَتَّى يَسْمَعَ كَلامَ اللهِ ثُمَّ أَبْلِغْهُ مأمَنَهُ ﴾ [ التوبة : ٦ ] ومنها ما ثبت في الحديث الصحيح من أن الرسول معمله الا الله مخاطب ليلة المعراج ربه جل جلاله وفُرضت إذ ذاك عليه الصلوات الخمس . وأما التحقيق في معناها ، فاعلم أن الكلام في اللغة العربية يطلق على معنيين : أحدهما : الألفاظ المعبرة عن المعنى القائم بالنفس ، فتقول : هذا كلام فصيح ، وكلام واضح · ثانيهما : المعنى القائم بالنفس الذي من شأنه أن يعبر عنه بألفاظ ، وعليه قول الأخطل : إن الكلام لفي الفؤاد وإنم جعل اللسان على الفؤاد دليلا ومثله قول عمر رضي الله عنه : إني زورت في نفسي مقالة ، أي قومت
6 - Speech (al-kalam): It is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, exalted be He; by it He commands, forbids, and informs. It is expressed by the compositions He revealed to His messengers, such as the Qur'an, the Torah, and the Gospel. As for the proof of the establishment of this attribute for Allah, exalted be He, it is the definitive texts established in both the Book and the Sunnah. Among them is His saying, exalted be He: 'And Allah spoke to Moses directly' (Qur'an 4:164), and His saying, glorified and exalted be He: 'And if any of the polytheists seeks your protection, then grant him protection so that he may hear the speech of Allah, then deliver him to his place of safety' (Qur'an 9:6). And among them is what is established in the authentic hadith that the Messenger, [may Allah bless him and grant him peace] (marred OCR), addressed his Lord, glorified and exalted be He, on the night of the Ascension, and on that occasion the five daily prayers were enjoined upon him. As for the investigation of its meaning, know that kalam in the Arabic language is used for two meanings: One: the expressions that express the meaning subsisting in the soul; so you say: this is eloquent speech, and clear speech. Two: the meaning subsisting in the soul which is customarily expressed by expressions, and upon this is the saying of al-Akhtal: 'Indeed speech is in the heart, and the tongue is made a proof of the heart.' And similar is the saying of Umar, may Allah be pleased with him: 'I have composed in myself a statement,' i.e., I have arranged.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage defines the sixth divine attribute: speech (kalam). It states that kalam is an eternal attribute subsisting in Allah's essence. Through this attribute, Allah gives commands, prohibitions, and information. The attribute is expressed externally through the revealed scriptures (Qur'an, Torah, Gospel). The proof for this attribute is from definitive texts: the Qur'anic verse that Allah spoke to Moses directly (4:164), the verse that commands giving protection to a polytheist so he may hear the speech of Allah (9:6), and the authentic hadith about the Prophet's conversation with Allah on the night of Mi'raj and the obligation of the five prayers. The author then provides a linguistic analysis of the word 'kalam' in Arabic. It has two meanings: first, the actual uttered words (alfaz) that express an inner meaning; second, the inner meaning itself (al-ma'na al-qa'im bi al-nafs) that is expressed by words. This second meaning is supported by the poetry of al-Akhtal (who says speech is in the heart, and the tongue is its evidence) and by a saying of Umar ibn al-Khattab ('I composed in myself a statement' meaning arranged it internally). The distinction between uttered speech (kalam lafzi) and inner speech (kalam nafsi) is crucial for understanding the nature of Allah's speech as an eternal attribute, as opposed to the created letters and sounds of the revealed books.

Key Terms
الكلام
صفة أزلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Allah's speech is created or temporary.
Correction: The passage defines speech as an eternal attribute subsisting in Allah's essence, which is uncreated and eternal.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT mentioned as a proof for Allah's attribute of speech in the passage?
A) Qur'an 4:164
B) Qur'an 9:6
C) Hadith of Mi'raj
D) The Torah

Key Takeaway
Allah's speech is an eternal attribute proven by definitive texts from the Qur'an and Sunnah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you realize that you are engaging with an eternal attribute of Allah, not just a book? How would your khushu' (concentration) change if you truly believed that His speech has always been with Him?
?
Allah spoke directly to Moses and to the Prophet on the night of Mi'raj. He speaks to you through the Qur'an. Are you listening with the same seriousness as if He were speaking audibly? What would you do today to respond to His commands?
?
If Allah's speech is eternal and perfect, then the Qur'an you hold is not a human product. Does your daily engagement with it reflect that conviction? Commit to one concrete change in how you approach the Qur'an starting today.

The Two Meanings of Kalam in Arabic
Explains the two linguistic meanings of kalam and their relevance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two meanings of the word 'kalam' in Arabic: the uttered expressions and the inner meaning in the soul, and how this distinction applies to Allah's speech.

Core Idea
Kalam means both uttered words and inner speech; Allah's eternal attribute is inner speech.

After establishing the attribute of speech, the author now clarifies the linguistic ambiguity of the word 'kalam' itself. In Arabic, it can refer either to the actual spoken words or to the inner mental meaning that the words express. This distinction is crucial for understanding that Allah's eternal speech is not a sequence of sounds or letters, but an eternal attribute which the revealed Books express. The author supports this with classical Arabic usage, including poetry and a saying of Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two meanings
Read the author's explicit listing: first meaning is uttered expressions (ألفاظ), second is inner meaning (معنى قائم بالنفس).
2
Examine the supporting evidence
The poetry of al-Akhtal places speech in the heart, not on the tongue. Umar's saying 'I composed in myself a statement' shows internal speech.
These examples prove that 'kalam' can mean inner speech.
3
Apply to theology
How does this distinction resolve the question of whether the Qur'an is created? The physical book is created, but the eternal attribute it expresses is uncreated.

The author then provides a linguistic analysis of the word 'kalam' in Arabic. It has two meanings: first, the actual uttered words (alfaz) that express an inner meaning; second, the inner meaning itself (al-ma'na al-qa'im bi al-nafs) that is expressed by words. This second meaning is supported by the poetry of al-Akhtal (who says speech is in the heart, and the tongue is its evidence) and by a saying of Umar ibn al-Khattab ('I composed in myself a statement' meaning arranged it internally). The distinction between uttered speech (kalam lafzi) and inner speech (kalam nafsi) is crucial for understanding the nature of Allah's speech as an eternal attribute, as opposed to the created letters and sounds of the revealed books.

Key Terms
الكلام
الكلام النفسي
الكلام اللفظي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Allah's speech is only the uttered words of the Qur'an.
Correction: The passage shows that speech includes an inner, attribute-based reality (kalam nafsi) of which the uttered words are an expression.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which meaning of 'kalam' is illustrated by the saying of al-Akhtal?
A) Uttered words
B) Inner meaning in the soul
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The word 'kalam' in Arabic can refer to both uttered expressions and the inner meaning in the soul; Allah's speech is the latter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you speak, is your inner intention aligned with your outward words? How often do you say one thing but feel another? Ponder that Allah hears both your uttered speech and the silent words in your heart. What steps will you take today to purify your inner speech?
?

?
You claim to believe with certainty in the oneness of Allah, but what does your inner speech whisper when you are alone? Are there hidden doubts or associations that contradict your outward profession? Commit to examining your heart's speech and seeking refuge from hypocrisy.

The Eternal Attribute of Speech: Definition
Buti defines the attribute of Speech and its nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of God's attribute of Speech as an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence.

Core Idea
God's speech is an eternal attribute, not a created act.

Buti begins by defining the attribute of Speech (al-Kalam). He clarifies that it is an eternal attribute inherent in God's essence, through which He commands, forbids, and informs. This distinguishes it from human speech which is temporal and created.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the translation.
Notice that Buti uses a concise definition.
2
Identify the key elements of the definition
Look for the three aspects: eternal, subsisting in essence, and the functions (command, forbid, inform).
These are the core of the definition.
3
Understand how it is expressed
Buti says the attribute is expressed through revealed scriptures. Consider what that means.
The Quran, Torah, and Gospel are expressions of God's speech.

Source Text

٦ - ( الكلام ) وهو صفة أزلية قائمة بذاته تعالى، هو بها آمر وناه ومخبر، عبر عنها نظم ما أوحاه إلى رسله كالقرآن والتوراة والإنجيل. فأما دليل ثبوت هذه الصفة الله تعالى فالنصوص القطعية الثابتة في كل من الكتاب والسنة، منها قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَكَلَّمَ الله موسى تكليماً ﴾ [ النساء : ١٦٤] وقوله جل جلاله وإنْ أَحَدٌ مِنَ المُشركينَ اسْتَجَارَكَ فَأَجْرُهُ حَتَّى يَسْمَعَ كَلامَ اللهِ ثُمَّ أَبْلِغْهُ مأمَنَهُ ﴾ [ التوبة : ٦ ] ومنها ما ثبت في الحديث الصحيح من أن الرسول [؟] مخاطب ليلة المعراج ربه جل جلاله وفُرضت إذ ذاك عليه الصلوات الخمس.

A hadith about the Night of Ascension is also offered, where the Prophet (may God bless him and grant him peace) spoke with his Lord and the five daily prayers were prescribed. The Essence of the Dispute on God's Speech
The author identifies the point of agreement and disagreement between Mu'tazila and Sunnis on the attribute of speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise point of agreement and disagreement between the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunna regarding the attribute of divine speech.

Core Idea
The dispute is not about whether God speaks, but about whether His speech is a created thing or an eternal attribute.

This passage from al-Buti lays out the common ground and the dividing line between two major theological schools. Both affirm that God speaks, and both accept that the recited Qur'an is created. But they disagree on what lies beyond the words: is there an eternal attribute of internal speech, or is it reducible to knowledge and will? Let's explore the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to get the overall flow. Notice the author's structure: he first states the consensus, then presents Mu'tazila, then Sunni, then pinpoints the disagreement.
2
Identify the point of agreement
Find where the author states that all Muslims agree on something. What do they agree on? And what do they call it?
Both groups agree that God speaks and that verbal speech is created.
3
Locate the point of disagreement
Look for the sentence that says 'Here the Mu'tazila separated from the majority'. What is the exact nature of the split? What is the disputed name?
The author uses the term 'kalam nafsi' for the Sunni position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جوهر الخلاف بين المعتزلة وأهل السنة والجماعة : إذا علمت هذا ، فاعلم أنه قد ثبت الكلام لله تعالى بإجماع الأمة ، وتواتر النقل عن الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام ، أنه سبحانه وتعالى متكلم مع القطع باستحالة التكلم بدون ثبوت صفة الكلام. وهذا القدر من الإجماع لا خلاف لأحد من المسلمين فيه. ثم إن المعتزلة فسروا هذا الذي أجمع المسلمون على إثباته لله تعالى بأنه أصوات وحروف يخلقها الله في غيره كاللوح المحفوظ وجبريل ، ومن المعلوم أنه حادث وليس بقديم . ثم إنهم لم يثبتوا لله تعالى شيئاً آخر من وراء هذه الأصوات والحروف تحت اسم الكلام. أما جماهير المسلمين أهل السنة والجماعة فقالوا إننا لا ننكر هذا الذي تقوله المعتزلة بل نقول به ونسميه كلاماً لفظياً ونحن جميعاً متفقون على حدوثه وأنه غير قائم بذاته تعالى من أجل أنه حادث ولكنا نثبت أمراً وراء وهو الصفة القائمة بالنفس والتي يعبر عنها بالألفاظ وهي غير حقيقة العلم وغير الإرادة وإنما هو صفة مهيأة لأن يخاطب بها الآخرون على وجه الأمر أو النهي أو الإخبار تدل عليه الألفاظ وهي صفة قديمة قائمة بذاته تعالى ضرورة استحالة توارد الخواطر وطروء المعاني عليه كما هو شأن الإنسان. وهذا هو إسناد الكلام إلى الله تعالى وبه يفسر ما أجمع عليه المسلمون. وهنا افترق المعتزلة عن الجمهور إذ إنهم لم ينسبوا إلى الله تعالى صفة قديمة بهذا المعنى اسمها الكلام أو الكلام النفسي. فقد قالوا إن مدلول العبارات الذي أطلقتم عليه اسم الكلام النفسي راجع في الحقيقة إلى صفة العلم إن كان هذا المدلول خبراً وراجع إلى صفة الإرادة إن كان أمراً أو نهياً وقد علمت أنهم يرون الإرادة والأمر بمعنى واحد. أما العبارات نفسها فألفاظ حادثة مخلوقة من الله كما اتفقنا جميعاً فهي ليست صفة الله تعالى ولكنها مخلوق من مخلوقاته وليس الكلام إلا عبارة عن هذا. إذا تأملت فيما ذكرناه أدركت النقطة الخلافية بين المعتزلة وأهل السنة والجماعة وهي أن هنالك معنى لألفاظ القرآن يتكون منه الأمر والنهي والإخبار المتوجه إلى الناس وهو قديم. فما اسم هذا المعنى؟ المعتزلة اسمه العلم إذا كان إخباراً والإرادة إذا كان أمراً أو نهياً. الجمهور اسمه الكلام النفسي وهو صفة زائدة على كل من العلم والإرادة قائمة بذاته تعالى. وأما الكلام الذي هو اللفظ فاتفقوا على أنه مخلوق وعلى أنه غير قائم بذاته سبحانه باستثناء أحمد بن حنبل وبعض أتباعه فقد ذهبوا إلى أن هذه الحروف والأصوات أيضاً قديمة بذاتها وأنها هي المعني بصفة الكلام. ولا ندخل بعد أن عرفت نقطة الوفاق والخلاف في شيء من المناقشة والجدال اللذين قاما حول هذا البحث لاعتقادنا بأن الخطب أيسر من ذلك وإن كنا نعتقد ما ذهب إليه الجمهور من أن المعنى الذي هو مدلول العبارات اسمه
The Essence of the Dispute Between the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a: If you know this, then know that speech (al-kalam) has been established for Allah by consensus of the community and by successive transmission from the prophets (peace be upon them) that He, glorified and exalted, is speaking (mutakallim) with certainty that speaking is impossible without the establishment of the attribute of speech. And this measure of consensus is not disputed by any Muslim. Then the Mu'tazila interpreted this which the Muslims agreed upon establishing for Allah as sounds and letters which Allah creates in something else such as the Preserved Tablet and Gabriel, and it is known that it is originated (hadith) and not eternal (qadim). Then they did not establish for Allah anything else beyond these sounds and letters under the name 'speech'. As for the majority of Muslims, Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, they said: We do not deny this which the Mu'tazila say, rather we affirm it and call it verbal speech (kalam lafzi), and we all agree on its origination and that it is not subsisting in His essence (qaim bi-dhatihi) because it is originated. But we establish something beyond that, which is the attribute subsisting in the self (al-sifa al-qaima bi-l-nafs) which is expressed by words, and it is not the reality of knowledge nor will. Rather it is an attribute prepared (muhayya'a) for addressing others in the form of command, prohibition, or information, indicated by words. And it is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, due to the impossibility of the occurrence of thoughts and the occurrence of meanings in Him as is the case with man. And this is the attribution of speech to Allah, and by it is interpreted what the Muslims agreed upon. And here the Mu'tazila separated from the majority, for they did not attribute to Allah an eternal attribute in this sense called speech or internal speech (al-kalam al-nafsi). They said: The signification of expressions which you have called 'internal speech' actually refers to the attribute of knowledge if this signification is information, and refers to the attribute of will if it is a command or prohibition (and you know that they consider will and command as one thing). As for the expressions themselves, they are originated letters created by Allah, as we all agreed, so they are not an attribute of Allah but rather a created thing among His creations. And speech is nothing but this. If you reflect on what we have mentioned, you will perceive the point of disagreement between the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a: that there is a meaning for the words of the Qur'an consisting of command, prohibition, and information directed to people, and it is eternal. So what is the name of this meaning? The Mu'tazila: its name is knowledge if it is information, and will if it is command or prohibition. The majority: its name is internal speech (al-kalam al-nafsi), and it is an attribute additional to both knowledge and will, subsisting in His essence. As for speech which is the utterance, they all agreed that it is created and that it does not subsist in His essence, except for Ahmad ibn Hanbal and some of his followers, for they held that these letters and sounds are also eternal in themselves, and that they are what is meant by the attribute of speech. And we will not enter, after you have known the point of agreement and disagreement, into any of the discussion and debate that took place around this research, because we believe the matter is easier than that, although we believe what the majority went to: that the meaning which is the signification of the expressions is named
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a classification and explanation of the central dispute between the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunna regarding the attribute of divine speech. The author first establishes the agreed basis: all Muslims affirm that God is speaking, and consensus confirms that speech is attributed to God. Then the author explains the Mu'tazila interpretation: they restrict divine speech to created sounds and letters in something other than God, so speech is originated. Then the Sunni position: they affirm verbal speech as created but also affirm an additional internal attribute of speech (kalam nafsi) that is eternal and subsists in God's essence. This internal speech is the meaning expressed by words, distinct from knowledge and will. The author then pinpoints the exact disagreement: whether the meaning of the Qur'anic expressions is an additional attribute (kalam nafsi) or reducible to knowledge and will. Finally, the author notes the exception of Ahmad ibn Hanbal who held that the letters and sounds themselves are eternal. The author concludes by declining to engage in further debate, stating a preference for the Sunni position.

كلام
كلام لفظي
كلام نفسي
صفة
علم
إرادة
قديم
حادث
معتزلة
أهل السنة والجماعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The dispute is about whether the Qur'an is created or eternal.
Correction: The passage shows that both groups agree that the verbal Qur'an is created. The real disagreement is whether there is an eternal internal speech attribute.

Checkpoint

B) That God speaks and that verbal speech is created.

D) That the letters and sounds of the Qur'an are eternal.

Key Takeaway
The core dispute is whether the meaning expressed by the Qur'anic words is an additional eternal attribute (kalam nafsi) or reducible to knowledge and will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Mu'tazila reduced internal speech to knowledge and will. In your own life, do you sometimes reduce your relationship with God's speech to mere intellectual knowledge or to following commands, missing the living, dynamic conversation He intends? The Core Disagreement: Naming the Eternal Meaning
Buti defines the single point of disagreement on the naming of the eternal meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the disagreement between the Mu'tazila and the Sunni majority regarding divine speech is merely terminological, not about the existence of an eternal meaning.

Core Idea
Both sides agree the Qur'an's meaning is eternal; the dispute is what to call it.

In this passage, Buti asks us to reflect on the previous discussion and pinpoint where the sects diverge. He reveals that both Mu'tazila and Sunnis affirm an eternal meaning behind the words of the Qur'an. The conflict is only over its name: Is it a distinct attribute or reducible to knowledge and will? This passage clarifies the precise point of contention.

Guided Path
1
Reflect on the common ground
Read the passage and note that both sects agree there is an eternal meaning behind the Qur'anic words. This is the starting point.
Both sides affirm the meaning is eternal, not created.
2
Identify the two naming positions
Find how the Mu'tazila name this meaning (knowledge for reports, will for commands) and how the Sunnis name it (internal speech as a distinct attribute).
The ellipsis (...) shows brevity; the contrast is clear.
3
Understand the significance
Consider why the name matters: it determines whether speech is a distinct attribute or reducible to other attributes.
This impacts the entire doctrine of divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا تأملت فيما ذكرناه ، أدركت النقطة الخلافية بين المعتزلة وأهل السنة والجماعة وهي : أن هنالك معنى لألفاظ القرآن يتكون منه الأمر والنهي والإخبار المتوجه إلى الناس وهو قديم . فما اسم هذا المعنى ؟ المعتزلة : اسمه العلم إذا كان إخباراً ، والإرادة إذا كان أمراً أو نهياً ... الجمهور : اسمه الكلام النفسي ، وهو صفة زائدة على كل من العلم والإرادة ، قائمة بذاته تعالى .
If you reflect on what we have mentioned, you will perceive the point of disagreement between the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a: that there is a meaning for the words of the Qur'an from which command, prohibition, and report addressed to people are constituted, and it is eternal. So what is the name of this meaning? The Mu'tazila: its name is knowledge if it is a report, and will if it is a command or prohibition... The majority: its name is internal speech (al-kalam al-nafsi), and it is an attribute superadded to both knowledge and will, subsisting by the Essence of the Exalted.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage identifies the single point of theological disagreement. Buti asks the reader to reflect and see that there is an eternal meaning underlying the words of the Qur'an—comprising commands, prohibitions, and reports. Both sides agree this meaning is eternal. The dispute is merely terminological: what to call it? The Mu'tazila call it knowledge (for reports) or will (for commands/prohibitions), refusing to recognize a distinct attribute of speech. The Sunni majority call it internal speech (kalam nafsi), affirming it as a separate, superadded attribute beyond knowledge and will, subsisting in Allah's essence. Thus the disagreement is whether speech is reducible to other attributes or is an independent attribute.

Key Terms
النقطة الخلافية
الكلام النفسي
صفة زائدة
العلم
الإرادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila deny the eternal meaning behind the Qur'anic words.
Correction: The Mu'tazila affirm the eternal meaning but identify it as knowledge or will rather than a distinct attribute of speech.

Checkpoint
What is the single point of disagreement between the Mu'tazila and the Sunni majority according to Buti?
A) Whether the meaning behind the Qur'anic expressions is eternal or created.
B) Whether that meaning is called knowledge, will, or a distinct attribute (kalam nafsi).
C) Whether the Qur'anic words are created or not.
D) Whether Allah has attributes at all.

Key Takeaway
The core disagreement over divine speech is terminological: whether the eternal meaning is a distinct attribute (kalam nafsi) or merely an aspect of knowledge and will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you hear only the words, or do you perceive the eternal speech of Allah behind them? This lesson shows that the meaning is eternal and personal. How does that shift the reverence you bring to each verse?
?
The Mu'tazila reduced Allah's commands and prohibitions to mere knowledge and will. Have you ever treated a divine command as just good advice rather than the authoritative speech of the One who speaks? What would change in your obedience if you truly believed it is an eternal attribute?
?
The Sunnis affirm a distinct attribute of internal speech. Do you live as if Allah genuinely speaks — in a way that is real and beyond your imagination? Take a moment: when you read the Qur'an, are you listening to the Speaker, or just processing text?

Createdness of Spoken Words and Ahmad ibn Hanbal's Exception
Buti states consensus on createdness of words and notes Hanbali exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the majority consensus on uttered speech being created and the Hanbali view that letters and sounds are eternal.

Core Idea
Spoken words are created, but Hanbalis considered even the letters eternal.

Buti clarifies a key doctrinal dispute about the nature of the Qur'an. While the majority agree that uttered speech is created, Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal and some followers held a contrasting view. This lesson examines that exception.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice how Buti states the consensus first, then introduces the exception.
The passage is short but packed with doctrinal weight.
2
Identify the consensus and exception
Find what all parties agree on regarding uttered speech, and then pinpoint how Ahmad ibn Hanbal differed. The exception is that he considered letters and sounds eternal.
The difference is about whether the very words are created or uncreated.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself why this distinction matters. It affects how one views the Qur'an as eternal or created in its linguistic form.
This distinction has historical and theological implications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكلام الذي هو اللفظ ، فاتفقوا على أنه مخلوق وعلى أنه غير قائم بذاته سبحانه ، باستثناء أحمد بن حنبل وبعض أتباعه ، فقد ذهبوا إلى أن هذه الحروف والأصوات أيضاً قديمة بذاتها ، وأنها هي المعني بصفة الكلام .
And as for speech which is the uttered word, they agreed that it is created and that it does not subsist by His Essence, may He be exalted, with the exception of Ahmad ibn Hanbal and some of his followers, for they held that these letters and sounds are also eternal in themselves, and that they are what is meant by the attribute of speech.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage presents the consensus on the spoken aspect of speech (kalam al-lafzi). Buti states that all parties agree that the actual uttered words (letters and sounds) are created (makhluq) and do not subsist in Allah's essence. However, he notes an important exception: Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal and some of his followers held that even these letters and sounds are eternal (qadim) and that these very elements constitute the attribute of speech. This shows that Hanbalis (in the earlier period) did not distinguish between the eternal meaning and the temporal expression, but considered the actual Arabic words of the Qur'an to be uncreated.

Key Terms
الكلام اللفظي
مخلوق
أحمد بن حنبل
حروف وأصوات قديمة
صفة الكلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think all Muslims agree the Qur'an is uncreated in every sense.
Correction: The majority hold that only the eternal meaning is uncreated, while the uttered words are created. The Hanbali view extends uncreatedness to the letters themselves.

Checkpoint

B) Ahmad ibn Hanbal and some followers held the letters and sounds are eternal.
C) The Ash'aris hold it is uncreated.
D) No exception exists.

Key Takeaway
The majority see uttered words as created, but the Hanbali position considers even the letters and sounds of the Qur'an to be uncreated.

?
