The Word of God as His Eternal Decree
The author reinforces that God's word is His pre-eternal decree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the word of God is His pre-eternal decree by which He created and will fold up the universe.

Core Idea
God's word is His eternal decree, not a created thing.

The author reinforces the argument that the Qur'an is God's eternal speech by pointing to the cosmic significance of His word. He asks rhetorically whether anyone could be ignorant that God's word is His pre-eternal decree, by which all things exist. This lesson explores that affirmation.

Guided Path
1
Read the rhetorical question
Read the beginning of the passage where the author asks if there is any ignorant person who does not know that God's word is His pre-eternal decree. Notice the tone of incredulity.
The author is emphasizing that this is obvious.
2
Identify what God's word does
The author lists two actions: bringing the universe into existence and folding up the heavens and earth. Reflect on the power of God's word.
3
Connect to the previous argument
This reinforces the earlier point that the Qur'an cannot be created because it is God's eternal decree. Consider how this fits into the larger debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم هل في الجهال جاهل لا يعلم أن كلمة الله التي بها أوجد الكون كله ، وبها ستطوى السماوات والأرض ، والتي تكرر ذكرها في كتابه في أكثر من مناسبة ، إن إلا قضاؤه وحكمه المبرم القديم ، حتى يغيب ذلك عن بال أولئك العلماء الأعلام فلا ينتبهوا إليه ؟ ! و ما علاقة الخلاف الذي بين المعتزلة والآخرين ، بهذه المسألة ، وقد علمت أنهم جميعاً متفقون على أن ألفاظ القرآن حادثة وأن معانيه قديمة وأن خلافهم فقط في تسمية المعنى القديم : هل يسمى صفة الكلام ، أم يسمى صفة العلم والإرادة ؟ .. ثم إنه ليس عجيباً كل العجب أن ترى في المستشرقين أو المبشرين من يفــوه بهذا السخف رغم أن في رؤوسهم عقولاً يفكرون بها ، لأنها صنعتهم المعروفة .
Then is there among the ignorant any ignorant person who does not know that the word of Allah by which He brought the whole universe into existence, and by which the heavens and the earth will be folded up, and which is repeatedly mentioned in His book on more than one occasion, is nothing but His pre-eternal decree and decisive judgment, such that that should be absent from the minds of those eminent scholars and they not be aware of it? And what relation does the disagreement between the Mu'tazila and the others have to this issue, when you know that they all agree that the words of the Qur'an are created and its meanings are pre-eternal, and their only dispute is in naming the pre-eternal meaning: is it called the attribute of speech, or is it called the attribute of knowledge and will? Then it is not at all surprising that you see among the orientalists or missionaries one who utters this foolishness even though they have minds with which to think, because that is their known craft.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage consists of three parts. First, a rhetorical question reinforcing the previous argument: the word of God is His pre-eternal decree and judgment, by which He created the universe and will fold it up. No ignorant person would fail to know this, so it is absurd that the earlier scholars would have missed it. Second, the author clarifies the actual nature of the dispute between the Mu'tazila and other Muslims over the createdness of the Qur'an. He states that everyone agrees that the words (alphabets and sounds) are created, and the meanings are pre-eternal. The only disagreement is terminological: whether to call that pre-eternal meaning the attribute of speech (صفة الكلام), or to call it the attribute of knowledge and will (صفة العلم والإرادة). This reduces the dispute to a semantic issue, not a substantive theological division. Finally, the author makes a dismissive comment about orientalists and missionaries who utter such foolishness despite having minds, because they are known for that.

Key Terms
قضاؤه وحكمه المبرم القديم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A created entity
B) His pre-eternal decree and decisive judgment
C) The physical universe
D) The teachings of the Prophet

Key Takeaway
God's word is not a created thing but His eternal decree by which all things exist.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you realize that you are uttering Allah's pre-eternal decree—the very word by which He created everything and will end it? How does that change the weight you give to each verse?
?
If Allah's word is His decisive judgment, what does that demand from you when you hear a command or prohibition in the Qur'an? Will you treat it as a passing suggestion or an eternal verdict on your life?
?
The passage says even the ignorant should know this truth. What ignorance in your own heart has caused you to treat the Qur'an lightly? What will you change today to honour it as the eternal decree it truly is?

The Real Disagreement on the Qur'an
The author clarifies the actual nature of the Qur'an dispute and dismisses orientalist claims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the actual points of agreement and disagreement between the Mu'tazila and other Muslims regarding the nature of the Qur'an.

Core Idea
The dispute is merely terminological: both sides agree the words are created and meanings are pre-eternal.

After reinforcing his argument, the author clarifies the historical dispute on the createdness of the Qur'an. He shows that both the Mu'tazila and their opponents agree on the key facts: the words (alphabets and sounds) are created, while the meanings are pre-eternal. The only disagreement is whether to call that pre-eternal meaning the attribute of speech or the attribute of knowledge and will. This lesson explores that clarification.

This is a terminological dispute, not a substantive one.

Jesus is Not the Eternal Word 'Be'
Buti refutes the claim that Jesus is the eternal word by distinguishing the command 'Be' from its object.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between Allah's eternal word 'Be' and its created objects, and why Jesus is not the eternal word itself.

Core Idea
The command 'Be' is eternal; Jesus is its temporal object, not the command.

Buti responds to the claim that Jesus is the eternal word of God. He clarifies that the word 'Be' is eternal, but its object (Jesus) is created. Through a Quranic verse and logical analogy, he shows that if the object were eternal, all creation would be eternal. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Buti uses a sharp rhetorical style.
2
Identify the key claim being refuted
The claim is that Jesus is the eternal word (the word 'Be'). Buti rejects this. Find where he states his answer.
The refutation begins with 'يجيبهم قائلاً'.
3
Understand the distinction between word and object
Buti explains that the word 'Be' is eternal, but its object (Jesus) is not. Grasp this crucial separation.
The term 'متعلق الكلمة' means the object of the word.
4
Follow the logical argument from the verse
Buti quotes Quran 36:82 to show that the command 'Be' applies to all creation, including Jesus. Observe how he uses the verse to support his point.
5
Reflect on the concluding rhetorical question
The passage ends with a rhetorical question emphasizing that the word of Allah is His eternal decree. Consider why this is powerful.
This question highlights the absurdity of confusing the eternal word with its temporal effects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجيبهم قائلاً : إن كلمة الله تعالى هي قوله : كن ، ولئن كان معنى « كن » هذه قديماً فإن ذلك لا يقتضي أن يكون متعلقها أيضاً قديماً . ولقد علم العقلاء وعامة علماء العربية أن ابن مريم ليس هو نفس كلمة « كن » ولكنه متعلقها عيسى وإنما أخبر الله عن عيسى عليه السلام بالكلمة نفسها مبالغة في بيان هذا التعلق ومبالغة في تنبيه الذهن إلى أن خلقه إنما كان بمحض إرادة الله تعالى التي تمثلت في قوله : كن . ولو كان متعلق الإرادة قديماً مثل الإرادة نفسها ، لكان العالم كله قديماً أيضاً ، إذ هو ليس إلا نتيجة إرادته سبحانه وتعالى وقوله له : كن . ألا ترى إلى قوله تعالى ( إنما أَمْرُهُ إذا أرادَ شَيْئاً أَنْ يَقُولَ لَهُ كُنْ فَيَكُون ﴾ [ يس : ٨٢ ] فكما يقول الله تعالى لكل شيء يريد خلقه : كن ، فيكون . كذلك قال الله تعالى عن عيسى ابن مريم : كن فكان مخلوقاً ، وكما أن الأشياء كلها حادثة في خلقها وإن تعلق بها خطاب الله القديم، فكذلك عيسى ابن مريم عليه السلام حادث في خلقه وإن تعلق به خطاب الله القديم . ثم هل في الجهال جاهل لا يعلم أن كلمة الله التي بها أوجد الكون كله ، وبها ستطوى السماوات والأرض ، والتي تكرر ذكرها في كتابه في أكثر من مناسبة ، إن إلا قضاؤه وحكمه المبرم القديم ، حتى يغيب ذلك عن بال أولئك العلماء الأعلام فلا ينتبهوا إليه ؟ !
He answers them saying: Indeed the word of Allah Most High is His saying 'Be', and even if the meaning of this 'Be' is eternal, that does not necessitate that its object is also eternal. And the rational people and the generality of Arabic scholars have known that the son of Mary is not the very word 'Be', but rather its object is Jesus, and Allah only informed about Jesus, peace be upon him, by the word itself as an exaggeration in clarifying this attachment and an exaggeration in alerting the mind that his creation was only by the mere will of Allah Most High which was manifested in His saying 'Be'. And if the object of the will were eternal like the will itself, then the entire world would also be eternal, since it is nothing but the result of His will, Glorified and Exalted, and His saying to it 'Be'. Do you not see His saying Most High: 'His command, when He wills a thing, is only to say to it 'Be', and it is' [Ya-Sin 36:82]? Just as Allah Most High says to every thing He wants to create 'Be', and it is, likewise Allah Most High said about Jesus, son of Mary: 'Be', and he was created. And just as all things are originated in their creation even though the eternal speech of Allah attaches to them, so too Jesus, son of Mary, peace be upon him, is originated in his creation even though the eternal speech of Allah attaches to him. Then is there among the ignorant one who does not know that the word of Allah by which He brought the entire universe into existence, and by which the heavens and the earth will be rolled up, and which is repeatedly mentioned in His Book on more than one occasion, is nothing but His eternal decree and irrevocable judgment, so that this escapes the minds of those eminent scholars and they do not pay attention to it?!
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a claim (likely from Christians or misguided Muslims) that Jesus is the eternal word of God. Buti begins by clarifying that the word 'Be' (كن) is eternal, but its object (the thing created, here Jesus) is not eternal. He argues that if the object were eternal, then the whole world would be eternal, since it is also the result of that same command. He then quotes the verse from Surah Ya-Sin (36:82) which shows that the command 'Be' is applied to every created thing, including Jesus. Therefore, Jesus, like all other objects of that command, is created (hadith). He concludes with a rhetorical question emphasizing that the word of Allah is nothing other than His eternal decree, implying that no reasonable person should confuse the eternal word with its temporal creation.

Key Terms
كلمة الله
كن
متعلق الكلمة
حادث
قديم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Jesus is the eternal word itself (the attribute of speech).
Correction: Buti clarifies that Jesus is the object of the eternal command 'Be', not the command itself. The command is eternal, its products are temporal.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what is the meaning of 'the word of Allah' in the context of Jesus?
A) It is the eternal attribute of speech, which is Jesus himself.
B) It is the command 'Be', which is eternal, but Jesus is its created object.
C) It is the created words of the Torah and Gospel.
D) It is the name of Jesus.

Key Takeaway
The eternal word 'Be' is not to be confused with its created objects; Jesus, like all creation, is a product of that command.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever, even for a moment, attributed divinity or eternity to any creature—perhaps a saint, a leader, or even your own ego—by thinking their will or power is independent of Allah's command 'Be'? What does this lesson teach you about the absolute dependence of every being on that single word?
?
If the entire universe—including Jesus—exists only because Allah said 'Be', then what claim do you have to any ounce of self-sufficiency? How will you let this truth reshape your daily prayer, trust, and fear?
?
When you recite verses like 'When He wills a thing, He only says to it 'Be', and it is' (Ya-Sin 36:82), do you truly feel the weight that every atom, every breath, and every moment is sustained by that eternal command? What would change in your life if you lived with that awareness every second?

The Attribute of Life: Definition and Proof
Buti defines the attribute of life and provides scriptural and rational proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of life as an eternal attribute of Allah and its proof from scripture and reason.

Core Idea
Life is the foundational attribute that makes all other divine attributes possible.

Buti now turns to the seventh attribute of meaning: life (al-hayah). This attribute is not merely existence but a distinct eternal quality subsisting in Allah's essence. In this passage, he defines it and provides both scriptural and rational proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text and translation carefully. Notice how Buti defines life and then gives two proofs.
2
Identify the definition
What does Buti mean by 'life' as an attribute? How is it related to the previous attributes?
Life is an eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence.
3
Understand the scriptural proof
Look at the verse from Ayat al-Kursi. How does it demonstrate that Allah is alive?
Allah describes Himself as al-Hayy.
4
Understand the rational proof
Why does Buti argue that knowledge, power, will require life? Could those attributes exist without life?
He argues it is inconceivable for them to subsist without life.
5
Reflect on the implication
Life is necessary for other attributes. Why does this matter for tawhid?
It shows Allah's attributes are interconnected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٧ - ( الحياة ) وهي صفة أزلية قائمة بذاته سبحانه وتعالى يتأتى بها ثبوت الصفات السابقة . ودليلها من النقل قوله تعالى ﴿ الله لا إلهَ إلاّ هوَ الحَيُّ القَيُّومُ ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٥٥ ] وكونه حياً نتيجة لثبوت صفة الحياة له . ودليلها من العقل ما ثبت من اتصافه جل جلاله بصفة العلم والقدرة والإرادة وغيرها ، إذ يتصور قيامها إلا بمن ثبتت فيه صفة الحياة .
7 - (Life) And it is an eternal attribute subsisting in His Essence, Glorified and Exalted, by which the affirmation of the previous attributes is attained. Its proof from transmission is His saying Most High: 'Allah, there is no deity except Him, the Ever-Living, the Self-Subsisting' [Al-Baqarah 2:255], and His being alive is a result of the affirmation of the attribute of life for Him. And its proof from reason is what has been established of His being described, Majestic is His Majesty, with the attributes of knowledge, power, will, and others, since it is inconceivable that they subsist except in one in whom the attribute of life is established.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh attribute of meaning: life (al-hayah). Buti defines it as an eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence, through which the previous attributes (knowledge, power, will, etc.) are affirmed. He provides two proofs: scriptural and rational. The scriptural proof is the Ayat al-Kursi (2:255), which describes God as al-Hayy (the Ever-Living). He explains that God being 'alive' is a result of the attribute of life being established for Him. The rational proof is that the other attributes (knowledge, power, will) cannot be conceived to subsist except in a living being; therefore, life is a necessary precondition for those attributes.

Correction: Buti clarifies life is a distinct eternal attribute necessary for other attributes, not reducible to existence.

What is the rational proof for the attribute of life according to Buti?
A) The universe is living, so its Creator must be alive.
B) The attribute of life is known through revelation only.
C) Attributes like knowledge and power cannot exist except in a living being.
D) Life is the same as existence, so it is self-evident.

Key Takeaway
Life is an eternal attribute of Allah, proven by both revelation and reason, and it is the basis for His other attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The attribute of life is eternal and self-subsisting; it does not depend on anything. How does this contrast with your own life that ends? Does this realization move you to invest every fleeting moment in what pleases the One who never dies? What is one concrete action you will take today to live for Him?

Affirming Attributes and Negating Their Opposites
Buti summarizes the attributes of meanings and the duty to negate their opposites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that affirming an attribute for God necessarily requires negating its opposite, and that both affirmation and negation are obligatory based on transmitted and rational proofs.

Core Idea
Affirming an attribute for Allah requires denying its opposite.

This passage concludes the discussion on the attributes of meanings. Buti not only recaps that these attributes are proven by scripture and reason, but he also highlights a crucial theological duty: just as we must affirm these attributes, we must equally negate their opposites. This logical entailment is foundational for proper tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the two types of proof mentioned: transmitted (sam'i) and rational ('aqli).
Buti refers back to earlier explanations for each attribute.
2
Understand the principle of necessary negation
Buti states that negating the opposites of God's attributes is a necessary consequence (mustalzam) of affirming those attributes. For example, affirming power demands negating weakness.
This principle applies to all attributes of meanings.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself why this principle matters. It protects tawhid by ensuring no imperfection is associated with God, and it shows the harmony between reason and revelation.
Both affirmation and negation are wajib (obligatory).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهذه جملة صفات المعاني التي جاء بها الدليل السمعي ، وأيده الدليل العقلي حسب ما ذكرنا عند شرح كل واحدة من هذه الصفات . وكما يجب اعتقاد هذه الصفات لله عز وجل ، فإنه يجب اعتقاد سلب نقائضها عنه عز وجل إذ هو من مستلزمات ثبوت تلك الصفات
So this is the collection of attributes of meanings (sifat al-ma'ani) which the transmitted proof brought, and the rational proof supported it, according to what we mentioned when explaining each one of these attributes. And just as it is necessary to believe in these attributes for Allah, Mighty and Majestic, so it is necessary to believe in the negation of their opposites from Him, Mighty and Majestic, for that is among the necessary consequences of the affirmation of those attributes.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This brief passage serves as a concluding summary for the section on the attributes of meanings (sifat al-ma'ani). Buti states that these attributes have been established by both scriptural and rational proofs, as previously explained for each attribute. He then asserts a key theological principle: just as it is obligatory (wajib) to affirm these attributes for God, it is equally obligatory to negate their opposites from Him. This is because affirming an attribute necessarily entails denying its opposite; for example, affirming power implies negating weakness. This principle is foundational in Sunni kalam.

Correction: Buti makes clear that negating the opposites is equally obligatory, as it is a necessary logical consequence of affirmation.

Checkpoint

B) Because negation is easier than affirmation.

D) Because the Mu'tazila demanded it.

Key Takeaway
Affirming God's attributes logically requires negating their opposites; both are obligatory duties in Sunni theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The passage teaches that negation is a 'necessary consequence' of affirmation. In your own life, are there attributes of Allah you affirm intellectually without letting that logically shape your attitude—e.g., affirming His power but living as if other forces matter? What one attribute will you focus on today to ensure both affirmation and negation are alive in your faith?
?
If you were to deny an attribute, what would that imply about your belief in its opposite? Ponder the seriousness of neglecting negation: it could inadvertently allow a deficiency to be associated with Allah. How will you guard your heart against such carelessness?

Moral Attributes: Consequences of Attributes of Meanings
Buti defines moral attributes as the results of attributes of meanings and lists them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that moral attributes are the necessary consequences of the attributes of meanings and the seven specific moral attributes affirmed for Allah.

Core Idea
Moral attributes are not separate; they are the effects of God's essential attributes.

In the previous lesson, Buti discussed the attributes of meanings—the core qualities that subsist in God's essence. Now he turns to what he calls 'moral attributes' (al-sifat al-ma'nawiyya). These are not new independent realities but the logical results of those essential qualities. He then lists the seven moral attributes that follow from the seven attributes of meanings, and notes that even the Mu'tazila—known for their rationalist theology—did not dispute this classification.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition
Read the definition carefully: moral attributes are 'not more than results of attributes of meanings'. Grasp that they are not separate entities but consequences.
The word 'results' (nata'ij) is key.
2
Identify the seven moral attributes
Find the list of seven attributes: Powerful, Willing, Knowing, Hearing, Seeing, Speaking, Living. Note that these correspond one-to-one to the seven attributes of meanings discussed earlier.
The attribute of meanings 'power' (qudra) results in the moral attribute 'Powerful' (qadir).
3
Note the Mu'tazilite agreement
Buti points out that even the Mu'tazila agreed on attributing these descriptions to Allah. Think about why this is significant for Sunni theology.
The Mu'tazila rejected the attributes of meanings but accepted these moral attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢ - الصفات المعنوية . أما الصفات المعنوية فهي ليست أكثر من نتائج صفات المعاني ، أي هي الأحكام التي تترتب على ثبوت صفات المعاني . فهي كونه جل جلاله قديراً ، مريداً ، عالماً ، سميعاً ، بصيراً ، متكلماً ، حياً ، ولم يخالف المعتزلة في نسبة هذه [؟]
2 - The moral attributes. As for the moral attributes, they are nothing more than the results of the attributes of meanings, i.e., they are the judgments that follow from the affirmation of the attributes of meanings. So they are that He, Majestic is His Majesty, is Powerful, Willing, Knowing, Hearing, Seeing, Speaking, Living; and the Mu'tazila did not disagree in ascribing these [?].
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage defines the second category of divine attributes: the moral attributes (al-sifat al-ma'nawiyya). Buti explains that these are not independent entities but rather the necessary results (nata'ij) of the attributes of meanings (sifat al-ma'ani). In other words, once we affirm that God has the attribute of power (meaning), it follows that He is described as 'Powerful' (a moral attribute). He lists seven moral attributes corresponding to the seven attributes of meanings previously discussed: Powerful, Willing, Knowing, Hearing, Seeing, Speaking, Living. He notes that even the Mu'tazila did not disagree on attributing these descriptions to God. The passage breaks off mid-sentence at the end of the page.

Misconception: Moral attributes are independent divine attributes separate from the attributes of meanings.
Correction: Buti explicitly states that moral attributes are nothing more than the results (nata'ij) of the attributes of meanings; they are the necessary consequences, not separate entities.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Moral attributes (al-sifat al-ma'nawiyya) are the necessary consequences of the seven attributes of meanings, describing Allah as Powerful, Willing, Knowing, Hearing, Seeing, Speaking, and Living.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

How does this change the way you call upon Him in your most private moments? Will you begin your next du'a with the awareness that His attributes are rooted in His very self?
?
The Mu'tazila agreed on moral attributes but denied the attributes of meanings. Do you ever find yourself comfortable with describing God's actions (e.g., He is powerful) while being indifferent to the deeper reality behind them? What might you be missing in your understanding of Allah if you stop at the description without pondering its source in His essence?

The Divine Attribute of Life and Its Proofs
Buti defines Life as an eternal attribute and gives its revealed and rational proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the attribute of Life is considered an eternal quality of Allah and how both revelation and reason confirm it.

Core Idea
Divine Life is the foundation of all other attributes.

In this lesson, Buti explains the seventh divine attribute: Life. He shows that it is an eternal attribute subsisting in Allah's Essence, without which no other attribute could be established. Both the Qur'an and rational necessity point to this truth. Let's explore his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice how Buti begins with a definition, then gives two proofs, and ends with a principle.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the two proofs
Look for the revealed proof (Quranic verse) and the rational proof (argument from other attributes). Understand why each supports the attribute of Life.
The rational proof relies on the impossibility of knowledge and power without life.
3
Understand the final principle
Buti concludes that believing in these attributes requires also denying their opposites from Allah. Reflect on why this is logically necessary.
This ties back to the oneness and perfection of Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٧ - ( الحياة ) وهي صفة أزلية قائمة بذاته سبحانه وتعالى يتأتى بها ثبوت الصفات السابقة . ودليلها من النقل قوله تعالى ﴿ الله لا إلهَ إلاّ هوَ الحَيُّ القَيُّومُ ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٥٥ ] وكونه حياً نتيجة لثبوت صفة الحياة له . ودليلها من العقل ما ثبت من اتصافه جل جلاله بصفة العلم والقدرة والإرادة وغيرها ، إذ يتصور قيامها إلا بمن ثبتت فيه صفة الحياة لا فهذه جملة صفات المعاني التي جاء بها الدليل السمعي ، وأيده الدليل العقلي حسب ما ذكرنا عند شرح كل واحدة من هذه الصفات . وكما يجب اعتقاد هذه الصفات الله عز وجل ، فإنه يجب اعتقاد سلب نقائضها عنه عز وجل إذ هو من مستلزمات ثبوت تلك الصفات
7 - (Life) It is an eternal attribute subsisting in His Essence (glorified and exalted be He) by which the previous attributes are established. Its proof from revelation is His saying, 'Allah, there is no deity except Him, the Ever-Living, the Self-Subsisting' [Al-Baqarah 2:255], and that He is Living is a result of the establishment of the attribute of Life for Him. Its proof from reason is what was established from His description (mighty and majestic) with the attributes of knowledge, power, will, and others, for it is inconceivable that they subsist except in one in whom the attribute of Life is established. So this is the totality of the attributes of meanings which the transmitted evidence brought, and the rational evidence supported it, as we mentioned when explaining each of these attributes. And just as belief in these attributes of Allah (mighty and majestic) is obligatory, so too belief in negating their opposites from Him (mighty and majestic) is obligatory, because it is among the necessities of the establishment of those attributes.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage defines the seventh attribute, Life (al-ḥayāh), as an eternal quality inherent in the Divine Essence (qāʾimah bi-dhātih) without which no other attribute can be established. Buti provides two proofs: first from revelation, citing the verse 'Allahu la ilaha illa huwa al-Ḥayy al-Qayyum' where 'al-Ḥayy' indicates life; second from reason, arguing that since we have established that Allah possesses attributes like knowledge, power, and will, these cannot be conceived in a being that does not have life, so life must be an attribute. He then concludes that all these attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-maʿānī) come from divine revelation and intellectual reasoning. Finally, he states the general principle: one must believe in these attributes and equally deny their opposites (naqāʾiḍ) from Allah, as that is logically required.

Key Terms
الحياة (al-ḥayāh)
صفة أزلية (ṣifah azaliyyah)
قائمة بذاته (qāʾimah bi-dhātih)
صفات المعاني (ṣifāt al-maʿānī)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that rational proof is unnecessary for divine attributes, relying solely on revelation.
Correction: Buti shows that reason confirms revelation: the existence of attributes like knowledge and power logically requires life.

Checkpoint
What is the rational proof for the attribute of Life according to Buti?
A) It is mentioned in the Quran.
B) Because other attributes like knowledge and power cannot exist without life.
C) Because the Mu'tazila affirm it.
D) Because it is self-evident.

Key Takeaway
Life is an eternal attribute of Allah, proven by both the Quran and rational necessity, and it is the foundation for all other attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You say you believe that Allah is al-Ḥayy, the Ever-Living. But do you live your daily life as if your very existence is sustained by Him every moment? What would change in your actions and thoughts if you truly internalized that?
?
The passage proves that life is the foundation for all other attributes. If you neglect to glorify Allah as the Living, how does that affect your trust in His knowledge and power? Are you willing to let this truth transform your worship?
?
Since affirming life requires negating its opposite, do you fear death as an end, or do you hope to meet the Ever-Living? How does this hope shape your priorities and your repentance today?
